1Ô∏è‚É£ CONTROL_AUDIO.md (drop in control/CONTROL_AUDIO.md or control/CONTROL_AUDIO_AUDIOBOOK.md)
# CONTROL ‚Äì Audiobook Engine / Multi-Actor Voice System

Owner: Karl  
Depends on: Life OS app, Otto automation, external TTS/voice-clone API (e.g. ElevenLabs)  
Status: v0.1 ‚Äì scaffolding

---

## 1. Purpose

Build an **Audiobook Studio** inside the Life OS app that can:

1. Convert my manuscripts into **role-tagged scripts** with stage directions.
2. Map each role (NARRATOR, DAD, BAD_GUY, MOM, LITTLE_GIRL, etc.) to a **voice model**.
3. Call an external **TTS / voice cloning API** to render audio per chapter.
4. Let me **listen while I edit**, drop notes, and re-render specific scenes/sections.
5. Support a future upgrade path to:
   - hybrid human + AI narration
   - pro studio production using the same script markup.

This is primarily an **editing tool** and Life OS feature first, and an eventual **distribution pipeline** second.

---

## 2. High-Level Architecture

### 2.1 Components

- **Life OS frontend**
  - New section: `Audiobook Studio`
  - Features:
    - Book picker
    - Role/character manager
    - Tagged script editor/viewer
    - Audio player w/ notes

- **Life OS backend**
  - API endpoints for:
    - listing books & chapters
    - reading/writing tagged scripts
    - reading/writing `audio_control.yaml`
    - triggering audio renders
    - serving rendered audio files

- **Audio Engine (service/module)**
  - Can live inside Life OS backend as a module.
  - Responsibilities:
    - Parse tagged script
    - For each line:
      - resolve role ‚Üí voice model
      - send text + metadata to TTS API
    - Stitch segments into chapter-level MP3
    - Save to `content/books/<book_slug>/renders/`

- **Otto**
  - Automation + control-doc brain:
    - Turn raw manuscripts into role-tagged scripts.
    - Maintain `audio_control.yaml` skeletons per book.
    - Provide scripts to:
      - ‚ÄúRender all changed scenes since last edit‚Äù
      - ‚ÄúUpdate role tags based on character list‚Äù

---

## 3. Folder Structure

Target structure (within `residential_repo`):

```text
residential_repo/
  control/
    CONTROL.md
    CONTROL_AUDIO.md

  apps/
    life_os/
      backend/
        # (Python/FastAPI or similar)
      frontend/
        # (Next/React ‚Äì Life OS UI)
      ...

  content/
    books/
      example_book/
        manuscript.md          # raw text (no tags)
        script_tagged.md       # role-tagged & staged script
        audio_control.yaml     # role ‚Üí voice mapping + defaults
        notes.md               # edit notes while listening (optional)
        renders/
          ch01.mp3
          ch02.mp3
          ...

example_book is a template folder. Each real book gets its own slug folder.

4. Data Formats
4.1 audio_control.yaml (per book)


Defines roles and their default voice models + behavior.


Separates content (script) from performance (voices, tone, pacing).


See template in content/books/example_book/audio_control.yaml.
4.2 script_tagged.md (per book)


Markdown script with inline role tags and optional stage directions.


Format guidelines:


Each speech line starts with [ROLE] or [ROLE, modifiers...]


Narration uses [NARRATOR]


Stage directions in modifiers or on their own lines.


Example snippet:
[NARRATOR]
The wind curled around the ridge like a slow exhale.

[DAD, calm, slower]
"Son, you don't build a cabin to escape life. You build it to face it."

[BAD_GUY, low, cold]
"You really think you're still in control?"


5. Life OS ‚Äì Audiobook Studio Features
5.1 MVP Features


Book selection


List folders under content/books/


CRUD basic book metadata (title, slug)




Character / Role manager


Read/write audio_control.yaml


Add/edit roles (NARRATOR, DAD, BAD_GUY, MOM, LITTLE_GIRL, etc.)


Assign each role to:


a voice_model_id (from voice API)


default tone/pacing (optional)






Script view


Load script_tagged.md


Show segments grouped by chapter / scene


(Nice to have) Simple editing UI for tags & directions




Render controls


Button: ‚ÄúRender Chapter X‚Äù


Button: ‚ÄúRe-render selected section‚Äù


Show status: Pending ‚Üí Rendering ‚Üí Done


When done, expose chapter MP3 URL to the frontend player




Listening + Notes


Player for each rendered chapter


Text area / comments tied to timestamps


Append notes to notes.md or a per-book notes store in backend DB





6. Audio Engine Requirements
6.1 External API (initial assumption)


Use something like ElevenLabs (or similar TTS/voice clone API).


Config via environment variables:


AUDIO_API_BASE_URL


AUDIO_API_KEY




6.2 Rendering Pipeline (per chapter)


Backend receives request:


book_slug


chapter_id (or index)




Load:


content/books/<book_slug>/script_tagged.md


content/books/<book_slug>/audio_control.yaml




Extract relevant chapter section.


Parse line by line:


Get role + modifiers + text.


Resolve role ‚Üí voice_model_id (with defaults from YAML).




For each line / chunk:


Call TTS API to generate audio snippet.




Stitch snippets into a single chapter MP3.


Save as:


content/books/<book_slug>/renders/chXX.mp3




Return metadata for frontend:


file path / URL


duration


optional markers per line/segment





7. Otto Integration
Otto tasks to implement later:


Manuscript ‚Üí script_tagged.md


Input: manuscript.md or Google Doc export


Output:


script_tagged.md with [NARRATOR] and character tags


initial audio_control.yaml with discovered roles






Smart tagging


Use dialogue patterns ("..." + ‚Äúhe said‚Äù) to infer roles.


Insert [DAD], [BAD_GUY], etc. based on a character map.




Selective re-render


Track changed scenes/lines


Trigger the audio engine only for those sections


Update per-chapter renders incrementally





8. Constraints / Decisions


Primary goal: internal listening and editing, not immediate retail distribution.


Synthetic narration is fine internally and for direct/private distribution.


If/when we target Audible/ACX:


We can re-use the same scripts + stage directions


Swap the ‚Äúrenderer‚Äù from TTS ‚Üí human studio.





9. Dev Instructions for Cursor
When running in Cursor:


Create file structure:


Ensure content/books/example_book/ exists with:


manuscript.md


script_tagged.md


audio_control.yaml


renders/ folder






Life OS backend:


Add endpoints under something like /api/audio:


GET /api/audio/books ‚Äì list books


GET /api/audio/books/{book_slug} ‚Äì get book metadata & roles


GET /api/audio/books/{book_slug}/script ‚Äì fetch tagged script


POST /api/audio/books/{book_slug}/render/{chapter_id} ‚Äì trigger render


GET /api/audio/books/{book_slug}/renders/{chapter_id} ‚Äì get audio file URL / metadata




Implement an internal audio_engine module:


load_control(book_slug)


load_script(book_slug)


render_chapter(book_slug, chapter_id)




Stub TTS integration:


Have a mock that just creates silent audio or placeholder files first.


Later, wire to actual TTS/voice-clone API.






Life OS frontend:


Add a new section: Audiobook Studio:


Page layout with:


sidebar: book list + chapters


main: script view + render controls + audio player


role configuration (reads audio_control.yaml via backend)








Keep everything configurable:


External API credentials via .env / config.


No hard-coded paths; use a small path utility to refer to content/books.




Goal of this control doc: give a single source of truth so any tool (Cursor, ChatGPT) can reason about the Audiobook Engine consistently.

## 2Ô∏è‚É£ audio_control.yaml template  

Create this at:  
`content/books/example_book/audio_control.yaml`

```yaml
# Audio Control ‚Äì example_book

book:
  slug: example_book
  title: Example Book Title
  default_chapter_pattern: "ch{num:02}.mp3"

voices:
  # Core roles
  NARRATOR:
    voice_model_id: narrator_clone_v1
    description: "Karl, calm narration voice"
    pace: 1.0
    tone: neutral-warm
    volume: 1.0

  DAD:
    voice_model_id: dad_clone_v1
    description: "Dad voice ‚Äì deeper, slower, wise"
    pace: 0.95
    tone: wise-calm
    volume: 1.0

  BAD_GUY:
    voice_model_id: villain_stock_01
    description: "Antagonist ‚Äì low, cold, controlled"
    pace: 0.9
    tone: cold-menacing
    volume: 1.0
    fx:
      reverb: none

  MOM:
    voice_model_id: caring_female_stock_03
    description: "Mom voice ‚Äì warm and steady"
    pace: 1.0
    tone: soft-reassuring
    volume: 1.0

  LITTLE_GIRL:
    voice_model_id: child_stock_bright_04
    description: "Little girl ‚Äì light, innocent"
    pace: 1.05
    tone: innocent-lively
    volume: 1.0

defaults:
  # Used if a line has no explicit modifiers
  pace: 1.0
  tone: neutral
  volume: 1.0
  pause_between_lines_ms: 300

chapters:
  # Optional mapping for chapters to script sections
  # This is for the engine to know how to slice `script_tagged.md`.
  - id: 1
    label: "Chapter 1"
    start_marker: "<!-- CHAPTER:1:START -->"
    end_marker: "<!-- CHAPTER:1:END -->"
  - id: 2
    label: "Chapter 2"
    start_marker: "<!-- CHAPTER:2:START -->"
    end_marker: "<!-- CHAPTER:2:END -->"

You can just change the voice_model_ids once we actually train/receive them from the TTS provider.

3Ô∏è‚É£ script_tagged.md example
Create this at:
content/books/example_book/script_tagged.md
This gives Cursor + the engine an example of how dialogue + stage directions work.
# Example Book ‚Äì Tagged Script

<!-- CHAPTER:1:START -->

[NARRATOR]
The wind curled around the ridge like a slow exhale. Below the timberline, the cabin lights blinked on, one room at a time.

[DAD, calm, slower]
"Son, you don't build a cabin to escape life. You build it to face it."

[NARRATOR]
He leaned against the post, thumbs hooked in that same old work belt, eyes on the tree line instead of me.

[BAD_GUY, low, cold]
"You really think you're still in control?"

[NARRATOR, short_pause]
The voice came from the darkness beyond the woodpile, soft enough to make my skin crawl.

[LITTLE_GIRL, distant, shaky]
"Daddy? Who are you talking to?"

<!-- CHAPTER:1:END -->


<!-- CHAPTER:2:START -->

[NARRATOR]
The next morning, the mountain pretended nothing had happened.

[MOM, soft, near_whisper]
"Drink this before you start thinking too hard."

[NARRATOR]
Steam curled up from the mug, cinnamon and fear wrapped together.

<!-- CHAPTER:2:END -->

When you‚Äôre ready, you can replace this with actual book content and just keep the same patterns.

4Ô∏è‚É£ Cursor Prompt to Kick Off Implementation
When you‚Äôre in Cursor in residential_repo, you can paste something like this into a dev console/chat:
You are working in the `residential_repo` monorepo.

Goal: Implement the **Audiobook Studio** foundations for the Life OS app, based on `control/CONTROL_AUDIO.md`.

Steps:

1. Create the example book folder and templates:
   - `content/books/example_book/`
     - `manuscript.md` (empty placeholder)
     - `script_tagged.md` (use the example markup from CONTROL_AUDIO.md)
     - `audio_control.yaml` (use the template from CONTROL_AUDIO.md)
     - `renders/` (empty folder, used for audio outputs)

2. In `apps/life_os/backend/`:
   - Add an `audio` module or router that:
     - Lists books under `content/books/`.
     - Reads `audio_control.yaml` for a given book.
     - Reads `script_tagged.md` for a given book.
     - Has a stub endpoint to "render" a chapter that:
       - For now, creates a small placeholder MP3 file in `renders/chXX.mp3` (silent or tone).
       - Returns JSON with the path and basic metadata.

   - Suggested endpoints (you can adjust naming to match existing backend patterns):
     - `GET /api/audio/books`
     - `GET /api/audio/books/{book_slug}`
     - `GET /api/audio/books/{book_slug}/script`
     - `POST /api/audio/books/{book_slug}/render/{chapter_id}`
     - `GET /api/audio/books/{book_slug}/renders/{chapter_id}`

   - Implement the audio engine as pure Python functions that:
     - Load `audio_control.yaml` + `script_tagged.md`.
     - Locate chapter start/end markers.
     - Return the text segments that would be sent to TTS later.
     - For now, don't call any external TTS API; just simulate audio rendering.

3. In `apps/life_os/frontend/`:
   - Add a basic "Audiobook Studio" page that:
     - Calls `GET /api/audio/books` and lists available books.

## High-level intent

Otto is a provider-agnostic AI agent that lives with my files (repos, Google Drive, local storage). It should:

- Be able to run **without** any specific external AI provider hard-wired.
- Have a clean internal architecture: core, skills, config, CLI.
- Have built-in **health checks** for skills.
- Have a **repo audit meta-skill** that inspects the Otto repo and writes reports.
- Be **safe by default**:
  - Propose repairs and refactors instead of auto-applying them.
  - Log and structure everything so I can later wire it into a Life OS app.

For this pass, **do not wire real LLM calls yet**. We‚Äôre building the skeleton with clear extension points.

- Root = `residential_repo`

### 1.1 CONTROL_OTTO.md

Create `apps/otto/CONTROL_OTTO.md` with this content (verbatim, except fix any typos):

```md
# Otto Control Document

## Vision

Otto is a provider-agnostic AI agent that lives with my files (repos, Google Drive, local storage), not inside any one UI (ChatGPT, Cursor, etc.).

If any external AI tool becomes unavailable or too expensive, Otto still:
- Reads tasks from documents
- Executes scripts and skills
- Organizes outputs
- Proposes refactors and improvements to its own codebase

All logic, prompts, and configuration live in my repos where I own them.

---

## Architecture Overview

Otto has four main layers:

1. **Storage & Index Layer**
   - Knows about Google Drive documents and local repos
   - Maintains an index of:
     - Watched command docs
     - Important project paths
     - Last processed timestamps

2. **Brain Abstraction Layer**
   - An `LLMClient` interface (to be added later) with pluggable implementations:
     - OpenAI, Anthropic, local models (Ollama), etc.
   - No hard-coded vendor dependencies.
   - Active provider and model will be set in config.

3. **Orchestrator & Skills**
   - Orchestrator:
     - Scheduler (cron-like jobs ‚Äî later)
     - Command router (maps tasks to skills)
     - Run log (successes, failures, duration)
   - Skills:
     - Each skill implements a common interface with:
       - `can_handle(task)`
       - `run(task, context)`
       - `self_test()` for health checks

4. **Interfaces**
   - Command Docs (Google Drive) ‚Äî later:
     - Text-based instructions in structured format
   - Life OS API (later):
     - Otto will read/write tasks for my household/project Kanban
   - CLI:
     - Local commands like `otto run-sample` and `otto health` for direct execution and debugging

---

## Safety & Ownership Principles

1. All logic lives in my repos (e.g., `apps/otto`).
2. All configs, prompts, and skills are files that I can edit with a normal text editor.
3. Data stays in my cloud and local storage (Drive, local disks).
4. Otto never auto-applies code or repo changes unless explicitly configured.
5. Every potentially destructive action should be:
   - Logged
   - Reversible (via git branch or commit)
   - Proposed first, then optionally applied

---

  - Running sample tasks

## Health Checks & Self-Repair

### Skill Health Checks

Every skill must implement `self_test()`:

- Input: no arguments (uses internal knowledge / config).
- Output: list of issues (empty list means healthy).
- Typical checks:
  - Required paths exist
  - Config values are present
  - Basic dry-run against test input (if cheap)

A health check runner will:

- Iterate over all skills
- Collect and log issues
- Optionally summarize them
- Write reports to `reports/skill_health_YYYY-MM-DD.md` (later; for now, just print + basic file output)

### Self-Repair (Proposal First)

Repairs must be **proposal-based** by default.

Safety config (in `otto_config.yaml`):

```yaml
safety:
  auto_apply_repairs: false
  auto_refactor_repo: false


When issues are detected:

Otto may later (with LLM support) generate:

Suggested patches or PR-style diffs

For now, Otto should:

Structure any proposed changes as Markdown notes

Write them to reports/repairs/ for manual review

No changes are auto-applied until I explicitly enable them or run a dedicated command.

Responsibilities:

Identify:

Dead/empty directories

Very large files

Skills without self_test

Create a structured summary of findings.

Produce a report under reports/audits/otto_audit_YYYY-MM-DD.md with:

Summary

Detected issues

# apps/life_os/tax/models.py

from sqlalchemy import (
    Column, Integer, String, Boolean, DateTime, Enum, ForeignKey, Float, JSON
)
from sqlalchemy.orm import relationship
from datetime import datetime

from apps.core.db import Base  # adjust import to your actual db module
from .enums import FilingStatusEnum


class TaxProfile(Base):
    __tablename__ = "tax_profiles"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)
    user_id = Column(Integer, index=True, nullable=False)  # link to your users table
    filing_status = Column(Enum(FilingStatusEnum), nullable=False)

    primary_state = Column(String, nullable=False)  # e.g. "ID", "MT"
    additional_states = Column(JSON, nullable=True)  # list of state codes

    has_home_mortgage = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    has_property_tax = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    has_business_income = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    has_hsa = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    has_fsa = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    has_student_loans = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    has_529 = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    has_charitable_giving = Column(Boolean, default=False)

    dependents = Column(JSON, nullable=True)
    # Example: [{"name": "Audrey", "dob": "2012-05-01", "relationship": "daughter"}]

    created_at = Column(DateTime, default=datetime.utcnow)
    updated_at = Column(DateTime, default=datetime.utcnow, onupdate=datetime.utcnow)

2.2 Tax categories & rules
Generic ‚Äúbuckets‚Äù for deductions/lines and the rules to categorize transactions.
# apps/life_os/tax/enums.py

import enum

class FilingStatusEnum(str, enum.Enum):
    SINGLE = "single"
    MARRIED_FILING_JOINT = "married_filing_joint"
    MARRIED_FILING_SEPARATE = "married_filing_separate"
    HOH = "head_of_household"

class TaxBucketEnum(str, enum.Enum):
    NONE = "none"
    W2_WAGES = "w2_wages"
    BUSINESS_INCOME = "business_income"
    BUSINESS_EXPENSE = "business_expense"
    MORTGAGE_INTEREST = "mortgage_interest"
    PROPERTY_TAX = "property_tax"
    CHARITABLE = "charitable"
    MEDICAL = "medical"
    EDUCATION = "education"
    RETIREMENT = "retirement"
    HSA = "hsa"
    CHILDCARE = "childcare"
    INVESTMENT_INCOME = "investment_income"
    OTHER_INCOME = "other_income"


class TaxDocumentTypeEnum(str, enum.Enum):
    W2 = "w2"
    FORM_1099_MISC = "1099_misc"
    FORM_1099_NEC = "1099_nec"
    FORM_1099_INT = "1099_int"
    FORM_1099_DIV = "1099_div"
    FORM_1098 = "1098"           # mortgage interest
    FORM_1098_T = "1098_t"       # tuition
    FORM_1098_E = "1098_e"       # student loan interest
    STATEMENT = "statement"      # general statement

# apps/life_os/tax/models.py (continued)

class TaxCategory(Base):
    __tablename__ = "tax_categories"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)
    name = Column(String, nullable=False)         # "Business: Tools & Equipment"
    bucket = Column(Enum(TaxBucketEnum), nullable=False)
    schedule_hint = Column(String, nullable=True) # e.g. "Schedule C, Line 22"
    description = Column(String, nullable=True)
    is_active = Column(Boolean, default=True)


class TaxRule(Base):
    """
    Simple rule engine for auto-categorization.
    Example: if vendor contains 'HOME DEPOT' and tagged as business ‚Üí Business Tools.
    """
    __tablename__ = "tax_rules"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)
    user_id = Column(Integer, index=True, nullable=False)

    # Simple string matching to start
    vendor_contains = Column(String, nullable=True)  # e.g. "HOME DEPOT"
    description_contains = Column(String, nullable=True)

    min_amount = Column(Float, nullable=True)
    max_amount = Column(Float, nullable=True)

    default_tax_category_id = Column(Integer, ForeignKey("tax_categories.id"), nullable=False)

    applies_to_business = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    applies_to_personal = Column(Boolean, default=True)

    priority = Column(Integer, default=100)  # lower = higher priority

    tax_category = relationship("TaxCategory")

2.3 Transactions (money in/out with tax overlays)
If you already have a transactions table, you can add these tax fields to it; otherwise:
class Transaction(Base):
    __tablename__ = "transactions"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)
    user_id = Column(Integer, index=True, nullable=False)

    date = Column(DateTime, nullable=False)
    amount = Column(Float, nullable=False)  # + for income, - for expense
    account = Column(String, nullable=True) # "Checking", "Visa 1234"
    vendor = Column(String, nullable=True)
    description = Column(String, nullable=True)
    source = Column(String, nullable=True)  # "plaid", "csv", "manual"

    # Basic general category
    category = Column(String, nullable=True)

    # Tax brain overlay
    tax_category_id = Column(Integer, ForeignKey("tax_categories.id"), nullable=True)
    bucket = Column(Enum(TaxBucketEnum), default=TaxBucketEnum.NONE, nullable=False)
    schedule_hint = Column(String, nullable=True)
    is_business = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    is_tax_relevant = Column(Boolean, default=False)

    tax_category = relationship("TaxCategory")

class TaxYearSummary(Base):
    __tablename__ = "tax_year_summaries"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)
    user_id = Column(Integer, index=True, nullable=False)
    year = Column(Integer, nullable=False)

    # Totals (stored as JSON to keep schema flexible)
    bucket_totals = Column(JSON, nullable=False, default=dict)
    category_totals = Column(JSON, nullable=False, default=dict)

    generated_at = Column(DateTime, default=datetime.utcnow)
    notes = Column(String, nullable=True)


class TaxDocument(Base):
    __tablename__ = "tax_documents"

    id = Column(Integer, primary_key=True)
    user_id = Column(Integer, index=True, nullable=False)
    year = Column(Integer, nullable=False)

    doc_type = Column(Enum(TaxDocumentTypeEnum), nullable=False)
    issuer_name = Column(String, nullable=False)  # "ACC", "Chase", "Mortgage Co."
    expected = Column(Boolean, default=True)
    received = Column(Boolean, default=False)
    received_at = Column(DateTime, nullable=True)

    storage_url = Column(String, nullable=True)  # link to GDrive / S3
    raw_metadata = Column(JSON, nullable=True)


3. Rule engine & flows
3.1 Rule engine skeleton
# apps/life_os/tax/rules.py

from typing import List, Optional
from .models import TaxRule, Transaction
from .enums import TaxBucketEnum

def apply_rules_to_transaction(
    tx: Transaction,
    rules: List[TaxRule],
) -> Transaction:
    """
    Mutates tx in memory; caller is responsible for persisting.
    """
    matching_rule: Optional[TaxRule] = None

    for rule in sorted(rules, key=lambda r: r.priority):
        if not rule_matches_transaction(rule, tx):
            continue
        matching_rule = rule
        break

    if matching_rule:
        tx.tax_category = matching_rule.tax_category
        tx.tax_category_id = matching_rule.default_tax_category_id
        tx.bucket = matching_rule.tax_category.bucket
        tx.schedule_hint = matching_rule.tax_category.schedule_hint
        tx.is_tax_relevant = matching_rule.tax_category.bucket != TaxBucketEnum.NONE
        # Very simple: if amount > 0 treat as income, < 0 as expense;
        # You can refine later.
    else:
        tx.is_tax_relevant = False
        tx.bucket = TaxBucketEnum.NONE

    return tx


def rule_matches_transaction(rule: TaxRule, tx: Transaction) -> bool:
    if rule.vendor_contains:
        if not (tx.vendor or "").upper().__contains__(rule.vendor_contains.upper()):
            return False

    if rule.description_contains:
        if not (tx.description or "").upper().__contains__(rule.description_contains.upper()):
            return False

    if rule.min_amount is not None and abs(tx.amount) < rule.min_amount:
        return False

    if rule.max_amount is not None and abs(tx.amount) > rule.max_amount:
        return False

    # Could later respect applies_to_business / personal with tx.is_business
    return True

3.2 Year-end package generator
# apps/life_os/tax/reports.py

from collections import defaultdict
from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from datetime import datetime
from .models import Transaction, TaxYearSummary
from .enums import TaxBucketEnum


def generate_tax_year_summary(
    db: Session,
    user_id: int,
    year: int,
) -> TaxYearSummary:
    start = datetime(year, 1, 1)
    end = datetime(year + 1, 1, 1)

    txs = (
        db.query(Transaction)
        .filter(
            Transaction.user_id == user_id,
            Transaction.date >= start,
            Transaction.date < end,
            Transaction.is_tax_relevant == True,
        )
        .all()
    )

    bucket_totals = defaultdict(float)
    category_totals = defaultdict(float)

    for tx in txs:
        key_bucket = tx.bucket.value if isinstance(tx.bucket, TaxBucketEnum) else str(tx.bucket)
        bucket_totals[key_bucket] += tx.amount

        if tx.tax_category:
            key_cat = tx.tax_category.name
        else:
            key_cat = "Uncategorized"
        category_totals[key_cat] += tx.amount

    summary = TaxYearSummary(
        user_id=user_id,
        year=year,
        bucket_totals=dict(bucket_totals),
        category_totals=dict(category_totals),
    )

    db.add(summary)
    db.commit()
    db.refresh(summary)
    return summary


4. Service layer: ‚ÄúTaxBrain‚Äù
This is what other parts of Otto call.
# apps/life_os/tax/service.py

from typing import List
from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from datetime import datetime

from .models import (
    TaxProfile,
    TaxCategory,
    TaxRule,
    Transaction,
    TaxYearSummary,
    TaxDocument,
)
from .enums import TaxBucketEnum
from .rules import apply_rules_to_transaction
from .reports import generate_tax_year_summary


class TaxBrain:
    def __init__(self, db: Session, user_id: int):
        self.db = db
        self.user_id = user_id

    # --- Profile ---

    def get_or_create_profile(self) -> TaxProfile:
        profile = (
            self.db.query(TaxProfile)
            .filter(TaxProfile.user_id == self.user_id)
            .first()
        )
        if not profile:
            profile = TaxProfile(
                user_id=self.user_id,
                filing_status="single",  # default; caller should update
                primary_state="ID",
            )
            self.db.add(profile)
            self.db.commit()
            self.db.refresh(profile)
        return profile

    # --- Transactions ingestion & categorization ---

    def ingest_transactions(self, txs: List[Transaction]) -> List[Transaction]:
        """
        Accepts Transactions already constructed, applies rules, persists them.
        (In practice, you'll probably pass in simple dicts and build Transaction objects here.)
        """
        rules = (
            self.db.query(TaxRule)
            .filter(TaxRule.user_id == self.user_id)
            .all()
        )

        for tx in txs:
            tx.user_id = self.user_id
            apply_rules_to_transaction(tx, rules)
            self.db.add(tx)

        self.db.commit()
        return txs

    def recategorize_all_for_year(self, year: int):
        rules = (
            self.db.query(TaxRule)
            .filter(TaxRule.user_id == self.user_id)
            .all()
        )
        start = datetime(year, 1, 1)
        end = datetime(year + 1, 1, 1)

        txs = (
            self.db.query(Transaction)
            .filter(
                Transaction.user_id == self.user_id,
                Transaction.date >= start,
                Transaction.date < end,
            )
            .all()
        )

        for tx in txs:
            apply_rules_to_transaction(tx, rules)

        self.db.commit()

    # --- Yearly summary / package ---

    def build_year_summary(self, year: int) -> TaxYearSummary:
        # Also a good place to sanity-check expected docs vs. received
        return generate_tax_year_summary(self.db, self.user_id, year)

    def list_expected_documents(self, year: int) -> List[TaxDocument]:
        return (
            self.db.query(TaxDocument)
            .filter(
                TaxDocument.user_id == self.user_id,
                TaxDocument.year == year,
            )
            .all()
        )


5. API endpoints (FastAPI router)
Minimal endpoints so your ‚Äúlife OS‚Äù frontend + background jobs can talk to the tax brain.
# apps/life_os/tax/schemas.py

from pydantic import BaseModel
from typing import Optional, List
from datetime import datetime
from .enums import FilingStatusEnum, TaxBucketEnum


class TaxProfileIn(BaseModel):
    filing_status: FilingStatusEnum
    primary_state: str
    additional_states: Optional[List[str]] = None

    has_home_mortgage: bool = False
    has_property_tax: bool = False
    has_business_income: bool = False
    has_hsa: bool = False
    has_fsa: bool = False
    has_student_loans: bool = False
    has_529: bool = False
    has_charitable_giving: bool = False

    dependents: Optional[list] = None


class TaxProfileOut(TaxProfileIn):
    id: int

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True


class TransactionIn(BaseModel):
    date: datetime
    amount: float
    account: Optional[str] = None
    vendor: Optional[str] = None
    description: Optional[str] = None
    category: Optional[str] = None
    is_business: bool = False


class TaxYearSummaryOut(BaseModel):
    year: int
    bucket_totals: dict
    category_totals: dict

    class Config:
        orm_mode = True

# apps/life_os/tax/routers.py

from fastapi import APIRouter, Depends
from sqlalchemy.orm import Session
from typing import List

from apps.core.dependencies import get_db, get_current_user  # adjust to your auth
from .schemas import (
    TaxProfileIn,
    TaxProfileOut,
    TransactionIn,
    TaxYearSummaryOut,
)
from .models import Transaction, TaxYearSummary
from .service import TaxBrain

router = APIRouter(prefix="/tax", tags=["tax"])


@router.get("/profile", response_model=TaxProfileOut)
def get_tax_profile(
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
    current_user=Depends(get_current_user),
):
    brain = TaxBrain(db, user_id=current_user.id)
    profile = brain.get_or_create_profile()
    return profile


@router.put("/profile", response_model=TaxProfileOut)
def update_tax_profile(
    payload: TaxProfileIn,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
    current_user=Depends(get_current_user),
):
    brain = TaxBrain(db, user_id=current_user.id)
    profile = brain.get_or_create_profile()

    for field, value in payload.dict().items():
        setattr(profile, field, value)

    db.commit()
    db.refresh(profile)
    return profile


@router.post("/transactions/import", response_model=List[int])
def import_transactions(
    items: List[TransactionIn],
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
    current_user=Depends(get_current_user),
):
    brain = TaxBrain(db, user_id=current_user.id)
    txs = [
        Transaction(
            date=item.date,
            amount=item.amount,
            account=item.account,
            vendor=item.vendor,
            description=item.description,
            category=item.category,
            is_business=item.is_business,
        )
        for item in items
    ]
    saved = brain.ingest_transactions(txs)
    return [t.id for t in saved]


@router.post("/year/{year}/summary", response_model=TaxYearSummaryOut)
def generate_year_summary(
    year: int,
    db: Session = Depends(get_db),
    current_user=Depends(get_current_user),
):
    brain = TaxBrain(db, user_id=current_user.id)
    summary = brain.build_year_summary(year)
    return summary

Then plug router into your main app:
# apps/life_os/main.py
from fastapi import FastAPI
from .tax.routers import router as tax_router

app = FastAPI()

app.include_router(tax_router)

Thought for 29s
Short version: you probably can‚Äôt truly ‚Äúwake Cursor up‚Äù programmatically right now ‚Äì but you can build a nice little system where:

Any app drops tasks into a shared inbox (file/folder).

A tiny background script watches that inbox and pings you when there‚Äôs work.

You have a saved ‚ÄúCursor worker prompt‚Äù that tells Cursor to pull the next task from that inbox, do it, and mark it done.

So you leave Cursor open, you get OS notifications when there‚Äôs work, and when you flip to Cursor you just hit your saved prompt and it chews through the queue.

Reality check: what Cursor can / can‚Äôt do
As of now (and from how you‚Äôre using it):

‚úÖ Cursor can run long agents inside the editor.

‚úÖ Cursor can read/write files in your repo.

‚ùå Cursor doesn‚Äôt expose a ‚Äúwake me via API‚Äù you can call from outside.

‚ùå There‚Äôs no true push notification from Cursor itself.

So best attack is: external orchestrator + shared command inbox + standard ‚Äúworker prompt‚Äù inside Cursor.

Architecture I‚Äôd use for you
1. Pick a single ‚Äúcommand inbox‚Äù in your repo
You already like control/ docs. I‚Äôd do something like:

residential_repo/
  control/
    cursor_queue/
      2025-12-01_001_fix-prime-order-step2.md
      2025-12-01_002_add-yardage-widget.md
    CURSOR_QUEUE_INDEX.md
Each task file = ‚Äúone thing you want Cursor to do‚Äù.

Task file format (simple):

# Task: Fix prime-order finish flow bug

id: 2025-12-01_001
status: pending          # pending | in_progress | done | blocked
priority: high
app: catered-by-me
created_at: 2025-12-01T20:30

## Context
- Step 2 flow was just refactored to "one finish at a time".
- Some existing jobs load with missing finish library rows.

## Instructions
- Reproduce bug described in CONTROL.md section "Prime Order ‚Äì Step 2".
- Fix the bug.
- Update tests if they exist.
- Summarize changes at the bottom of this file under "Implementation Notes".

## Implementation Notes
(leave for Cursor to fill in)
Any app can generate one of these and drop it in control/cursor_queue/.

2. Write a tiny watcher that notifies you
A lightweight Python script can run on your machine (or in the background via Task Scheduler) and:

Poll the cursor_queue folder every X minutes.

Count status: pending.

When the count increases, send a Windows toast notification and maybe a ‚Äúding‚Äù.

Pseudo-code:

import time
from pathlib import Path

QUEUE_DIR = Path(r"E:\My Drive\residential_repo\control\cursor_queue")

def count_pending():
    pending = 0
    for p in QUEUE_DIR.glob("*.md"):
        text = p.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
        if "status: pending" in text:
            pending += 1
    return pending

def notify(message):
    # simplest version: just print or play a sound
    print(message)
    # you can hook into win10toast or PowerShell for real toasts

def main():
    last_count = count_pending()
    while True:
        time.sleep(60)  # check every minute
        current = count_pending()
        if current > last_count:
            notify(f"Cursor queue: {current} pending tasks")
        last_count = current

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
If you want proper Windows notifications, this script can call a PowerShell toast or use a Python library (win10toast, etc.).

Net effect: you‚Äôre working, a new app drops a task file ‚Üí watcher sees it ‚Üí bing ‚Üí you know ‚ÄúCursor has work.‚Äù

3. Standard ‚ÄúCursor worker prompt‚Äù
Now the magic: you save a prompt in Cursor (as a snippet or just pinned in a doc) that turns Cursor into a little worker that pulls tasks from the queue.

Something like:

CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md

You are a coding assistant working inside residential_repo.
Your job:

Open control/cursor_queue/ and find the first .md file with status: pending.

Set status: in_progress.

Read the task carefully and follow the ‚ÄúInstructions‚Äù section.

Make all necessary code changes, tests, and docs.

When done, update the task file:

Set status: done

Add a bullet list of changed files and a short summary under ‚ÄúImplementation Notes‚Äù.

Then move on to the next status: pending task and repeat.

When there are no more pending tasks, tell me: IDLE: no pending tasks.

Never invent tasks. Never skip updating the status in the task file.

Workflow:

You see a toast: ‚ÄúCursor queue: 3 pending tasks‚Äù.

You hit Cursor, open your CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT, run agent.

Cursor works through tasks, updating statuses, until there are none.

At the end it prints IDLE: no pending tasks.

Now you know it‚Äôs ‚Äúready for the next prompt‚Äù.

4. Let other apps drop tasks into the queue
Now we wire in your other systems:

Google Drive / Docs ‚Üí queue:
A small script (could run hourly) that:

scans a Drive folder for TODO_*.md or TODO_*.txt,

converts each into a proper cursor_queue task file in the repo,

marks the original as ‚Äúimported‚Äù.

Otto-generated apps ‚Üí queue:
In each app‚Äôs code, instead of just writing ‚Äúwe should fix X‚Äù into a log, it can write a .md file directly into control/cursor_queue/ on the shared drive.

Manual quick-add:
You can have a PowerShell function like add-cursortask "Fix header padding on SMB site" that writes a stub .md task file with that title and status: pending. The watcher picks it up and notifies you.

5. ‚ÄúWake Cursor up when it has things to do‚Äù
True auto-wake (Cursor starts agent by itself) isn‚Äôt really possible without hacks, but you can get 90% there:

Notification + focus script (optional):
Your watcher script can, on new tasks:

Show toast,

Optionally run a PowerShell command to bring the Cursor window to the foreground.

Auto-paste worker prompt (spicy hack):
If you really want, you can use AutoHotkey / PowerShell to:

Focus Cursor,

Simulate keystrokes to paste the worker prompt and hit Enter.
That‚Äôs hacky, but technically doable if you accept the jank.

For sanity, I‚Äôd start with manual agent trigger: notification + you hit a hotkey in Cursor to insert/run the worker prompt.

Thought for 25s
Yep, this is super doable, and we can keep it exactly in the shape you want:

You talk ‚Üí something listens ‚Üí standardized to-do item.

Cursor runs a ‚Äúdo the next task‚Äù prompt.

If Cursor can‚Äôt finish, it marks the task as blocked and that bubbles back up (and Otto can help).

You never need two screens to move stuff onto Cursor‚Äôs list.

I‚Äôll lay it out end-to-end and keep the extra stuff optional.

0. The flow we‚Äôre designing
Let‚Äôs anchor the exact flow you described:

You send a text or voice message (‚ÄúFix the recipe filters so I can sort by most recent‚Äù).

A bot in the middle:

transcribes (if voice),

converts that into a standard task format,

drops it onto a Cursor to-do list.

At some point, Cursor runs a ‚Äúworker prompt‚Äù that:

pulls the next task,

does the work,

updates the task as done OR blocked.

If a task is blocked (Cursor can‚Äôt finish), it:

gets flagged,

sends that upstream (notification to you, and/or to Otto to try to fix it or prepare a fix path).

You keep talking your list into your phone; Cursor/stack handles the pipeline.

That‚Äôs the core. Everything else is just picking tools to do those jobs.

1. Standard task format (the center of everything)
Let‚Äôs lock in a simple, consistent format first ‚Äî one file per task, living in a queue folder Cursor can read:

control/cursor_queue/2025-12-01_001_catered-fix-filters.md

# Task: Fix recipe filters sorting by most recent

id: 2025-12-01_001
status: pending          # pending | in_progress | done | blocked
source: voice            # voice | sms | app | manual
app: catered-by-me       # or smb_site, otto, personal, etc.
priority: normal         # low | normal | high | urgent
created_at: 2025-12-01T20:30:00
created_by: karl

## Raw Input
"Fix the recipe filters so I can sort by most recent and favorites. Right now it only does A‚ÄìZ I think."

## Parsed Instructions
- App: CateredByMe recipe library
- Goal: Add sorting by:
  - Most recent
  - Favorites
- Keep existing A‚ÄìZ sort if present.
- Update any tests or docs that reference sorting.

## Acceptance Criteria
- User can pick "Most recent" and "Favorites" sort options on recipe library.
- No errors in console.
- Existing tests pass or are updated.

## Implementation Notes
(For Cursor/Otto to fill in: changed files, summary, gotchas.)

## Blocked Notes
(Only used if status becomes `blocked`.)
Everything else in the system is just:

Writing these files.

Reading & updating these files.

2. Intake: text & voice ‚Üí ‚ÄúParsed Instructions‚Äù task file
2.1 Input channels
Pick at least one to start:

SMS number (Twilio, Google Voice + Zap, etc.)

Voice:

Call a number and speak,

Or record a voice note on your phone ‚Üí auto-upload to a folder.

You say things like:

‚ÄúCateredByMe: add a filter so I can search recipes by ingredient, high priority.‚Äù

or just:

‚ÄúFix the yardage calculator so it handles half yards correctly.‚Äù

2.2 Intake bot (the ‚Äúsomething in the middle‚Äù)
This is the piece that gives you the consistent structure without you thinking about it.

Responsibilities:

Transcribe voice to text (Whisper / any STT).

Optionally use an LLM (Otto / OpenAI) to:

turn the raw sentence into the Parsed Instructions + Acceptance Criteria,

guess app, priority, etc.

Generate a task file using the template above and save it into:

control/cursor_queue/<timestamp>_<slug>.md in your repo (on your shared drive).

You already have Otto and Python/FastAPI vibes going, so this looks like:

A tiny ‚ÄúIntake service‚Äù with one endpoint:

POST /intake with { text, source: 'sms' | 'voice' }

That service:

Calls LLM to convert text ‚Üí the task fields.

Writes the .md file into control/cursor_queue.

Example conversion:

You say:

‚ÄúSMB site: make the floor plan cards clickable and go to a details page. Medium priority.‚Äù

The intake bot turns that into:

app: smb_site
priority: normal
Raw Input: "SMB site: make the floor plan cards clickable..."
Parsed Instructions:
- On the Sugar Mountain Builders site home page, make each floor plan card clickable.
- Clicking should route to a floor plan detail page for that plan.
Acceptance Criteria:
- Clicking ‚ÄúBitterroot‚Äù floor plan goes to a /floorplans/bitterroot page with details.
...
You don‚Äôt see that; it‚Äôs just written for Cursor.

3. Cursor worker: executing the to-do list
This is your ‚Äútool or a me‚Äù that runs the prompt in Cursor and works the queue.

3.1 Worker prompt
Saved in control/CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md and/or as a Cursor snippet:

Cursor Worker Instructions

You are working inside residential_repo.
Your job:

Look in control/cursor_queue/ for .md task files with status: pending.

Pick the oldest pending task.

Open that file and:

set status: in_progress

keep Raw Input untouched

use Parsed Instructions & Acceptance Criteria to guide your work.

Make all necessary code/document changes to satisfy the task.

When you believe the task is fully completed:

set status: done

append under Implementation Notes:

list of changed files

short summary of changes

If you encounter something that prevents completion after reasonable attempts:

set status: blocked

fill in Blocked Notes with:

what you tried

why it‚Äôs blocked

what info or change is needed

After finishing a task (done or blocked), move on to the next status: pending task.

When no pending tasks remain, respond with:
IDLE: No pending tasks in control/cursor_queue.

Never invent tasks. Never delete tasks. Always update task status.

You run this when you want Cursor to chew through your backlog.

3.2 ‚ÄúNot getting stuck‚Äù
The key is explicit instructions about blocked state:

Cursor is allowed to say ‚ÄúI can‚Äôt finish this because X‚Äù.

But it must:

stop,

mark status: blocked,

explain why.

This sets you up for the escalation path.

4. Escalation: blocked tasks ‚Üí upstream + Otto
When Cursor can‚Äôt finish:

That task file moves to status: blocked.

Blocked Notes explains why.

Now another small bot (or the same intake service, different route) can:

Scan control/cursor_queue for status: blocked.

2. Standard task file format (center of the universe)
Drop this in control/CURSOR_TASK_TEMPLATE.md:

# Task: <Short, imperative title>

id: <YYYY-MM-DD_seq_slug>      # e.g. 2025-12-01_001_catered-filters
status: pending                # pending | in_progress | done | blocked
source: <voice|sms|app|manual>
app: <catered-by-me|smb_site|otto|personal>
priority: normal               # low | normal | high | urgent
created_at: <ISO8601 timestamp>
created_by: karl

## Raw Input
<Original text or voice transcript here>

## Parsed Instructions
- <bullet list of concrete steps for Cursor to follow>
- ...

## Acceptance Criteria
- <clear, testable criteria>
- ...

## Implementation Notes
(For Cursor/Otto to fill in: changed files, summary, gotchas.)

## Blocked Notes
(For Cursor to fill in if status becomes `blocked`:
- What was tried
- Why it failed
- What‚Äôs needed to proceed
)
Every task in control/cursor_queue/*.md follows this.

3. Cursor worker prompt (with built-in ‚Äúblocked‚Äù behavior)
Paste this into control/CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md and save as a snippet in Cursor:

Cursor Worker Instructions ‚Äì Queue Runner

You are working inside residential_repo on my local machine.
Your job is to execute tasks from the file-based queue.

Look in control/cursor_queue/ for files ending in .md.

Open each file and find those with status: pending.

Choose the oldest pending task based on its id or filename.

In that task file:

Change status: pending to status: in_progress.

Do not edit Raw Input.

Use Parsed Instructions and Acceptance Criteria as the source of truth.

Make all necessary code and documentation changes in the repo to complete the task.

When you believe the task is fully completed:

Change status: in_progress to status: done.

Under Implementation Notes, add:

- Changed files: <list of files>

- Summary: <short description of what you did>

If you cannot complete the task after reasonable attempts because something is missing or broken:

Change status: in_progress to status: blocked.

Under Blocked Notes, add:

What you tried (steps and files touched)

Why it is blocked (e.g., missing API key, unknown design decision, failing tests you cannot interpret)

What is needed to unblock it.

After updating that task file, repeat the process from step 1 until there are no more tasks with status: pending.

When no pending tasks remain, respond with:
IDLE: No pending tasks in control/cursor_queue.

Never create or delete task files. Only update status, Implementation Notes, and Blocked Notes in existing tasks.

That‚Äôs your Cursor side, done.

6. Watcher / notifier with test + repair loop
This is the bit you ‚Äújust leave running‚Äù that watches the queue and flagged tasks.

6.1 Core loop
Pseudo-Python:

from pathlib import Path
import time

QUEUE_DIR = Path(r"E:\My Drive\residential_repo\control\cursor_queue")

def count_tasks_by_status():
    counts = {"pending": 0, "blocked": 0}
    for p in QUEUE_DIR.glob("*.md"):
        text = p.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
        for status in counts.keys():
            if f"status: {status}" in text:
                counts[status] += 1
                break
    return counts

def notify(message):
    print(message)  # later: Windows toast, sound, Discord webhook, etc.

def watcher_loop():
    last_counts = count_tasks_by_status()
    notify(f"Cursor queue watcher started. Pending={last_counts['pending']}, Blocked={last_counts['blocked']}")
    while True:
        time.sleep(60)
        counts = count_tasks_by_status()
        if counts["pending"] > last_counts["pending"]:
            notify(f"New Cursor tasks available: {counts['pending']} pending")
        if counts["blocked"] > last_counts["blocked"]:
            notify(f"New BLOCKED tasks: {counts['blocked']} total")
        last_counts = counts
6.2 Test + repair for the watcher
Before entering watcher_loop, run:

def check_queue_dir():
    if not QUEUE_DIR.exists():
        return False, "Queue directory missing"
    if not QUEUE_DIR.is_dir():
        return False, "Queue path is not a directory"
    return True, "Queue directory OK"

def repair_queue_dir():
    # Try to create if missing
    try:
        QUEUE_DIR.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        return True, "Queue directory created"
    except Exception as e:
        return False, f"Failed to create queue directory: {e}"

def check_and_repair_queue_dir():
    ok, msg = check_queue_dir()
    if ok:
        print(msg)
        return True
    print(f"[WARN] {msg}, attempting repair...")
    ok, rmsg = repair_queue_dir()
    print(("[OK] " if ok else "[ERROR] ") + rmsg)
    return ok
The orchestrator command calls check_and_repair_queue_dir() before starting the watcher. If that fails, it exits with a clear error.

1. CONTROL doc ‚Äì control/CONTROL_CURSOR_PIPELINE.md
Create this file in your repo:

# CONTROL ‚Äì Cursor Task Pipeline

## Purpose

Turn messy human input (voice, text, meetings) into a structured queue of tasks that Cursor can execute without me manually copy/pasting between screens.

High-level flow:

1. Input:
   - Text (SMS / chat)
   - Voice notes / voicemail
   - Meeting recordings / long transcripts

2. Intake service:
   - Transcribes audio (if needed)
   - Uses an LLM to convert input ‚Üí standardized Markdown task files
   - Writes tasks into `control/cursor_queue/`

3. Cursor worker:
   - Uses a saved "Cursor Worker" prompt
   - Pulls tasks from the queue
   - Makes code changes
   - Marks tasks `done` or `blocked`

4. Watcher / Escalator:
   - Watches the queue for new `pending` or `blocked` tasks
   - Notifies me when there is work or when something is stuck
   - Optionally calls Otto to help triage blocked tasks


## Folder structure

```text
residential_repo/
  control/
    CONTROL_CURSOR_PIPELINE.md        <- this control doc
    CURSOR_TASK_TEMPLATE.md           <- template for a single task
    CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md           <- prompt for Cursor agent
    cursor_queue/                     <- one .md file per task
      2025-12-01_001_catered-filters.md
      2025-12-01_002_smb-floorplan-details.md
  scripts/
    manage_cursor_pipeline.py         <- orchestrator script (watcher + health checks)
Task lifecycle
Each task is a Markdown file in control/cursor_queue/ that follows CURSOR_TASK_TEMPLATE.md.

Statuses:

pending ‚Äì created by the intake service, waiting for Cursor

in_progress ‚Äì currently being worked on by Cursor

done ‚Äì successfully completed

blocked ‚Äì Cursor attempted work but could not finish; requires attention

All tools must only update status, Implementation Notes, and Blocked Notes. No tool is allowed to silently delete tasks.

Components
1. Intake service
Responsibilities:

Receive input from:

SMS / text

Voice notes / voicemail

Uploaded meeting recordings

Transcribe audio ‚Üí text (if needed)

Call an LLM with:

Single-input prompt (voice/text ‚Üí one task) or

Meeting prompt (long transcript ‚Üí many tasks)

Create .md files in control/cursor_queue/ using the template

Endpoints (example):

POST /intake/single ‚Äì JSON { "source": "sms|voice|manual", "text": "..." }

POST /intake/meeting ‚Äì JSON { "source": "meeting", "transcript": "..." }

GET /health ‚Äì returns 200/OK if configured

Environment it needs:

OPENAI_API_KEY (or equivalent for Otto‚Äôs LLM calls)

Path to the repo root (e.g. REPO_ROOT=E:\My Drive\residential_repo)

2. Cursor Worker
Uses control/CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md inside Cursor.

Behavior:

Scan control/cursor_queue/ for .md files with status: pending

Take the oldest one, set in_progress

Do the work based on Parsed Instructions and Acceptance Criteria

Set status: done and fill out Implementation Notes

If it can‚Äôt finish:

Set status: blocked

Fill out Blocked Notes

Repeat until no pending remain

Finally respond: IDLE: No pending tasks in control/cursor_queue.

3. Watcher / Notifier
Script in scripts/manage_cursor_pipeline.py:

Validates:

Repo path exists

control/cursor_queue/ exists (creates if missing)

Environment keys are present

Intake service is reachable (/health)

Starts a loop that:

Counts pending and blocked tasks

Logs or notifies when counts increase

Future: integrate OS notifications / SMS / Discord

How to use (human workflow)
Start the pipeline:

cd residential_repo
python scripts/manage_cursor_pipeline.py
Add tasks:

Talk to Frat (ChatGPT) ‚Üí copy spec into intake app

Text a number / drop a voice note into the intake app

Upload a meeting recording for parsing

Let the intake service write tasks into control/cursor_queue/.

When at the computer:

Open Cursor in residential_repo

Run the "Cursor Worker" prompt from CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md

Watch it process tasks

If tasks are blocked:

Look at Blocked Notes in the task files

Optionally have Otto triage and create follow-up tasks

## 2. Task template ‚Äì `control/CURSOR_TASK_TEMPLATE.md`

```md
# Task: <Short, imperative title>

id: <YYYY-MM-DD_seq_slug>      # e.g. 2025-12-01_001_catered-filters
status: pending                # pending | in_progress | done | blocked
source: <voice|sms|app|manual|meeting>
app: <catered-by-me|smb_site|otto|personal|other>
priority: normal               # low | normal | high | urgent
created_at: <ISO8601 timestamp>
created_by: karl

## Raw Input
<Original text or transcript fragment that led to this task.>

## Parsed Instructions
- <Bullet list of concrete steps for Cursor to follow>
- ...

## Acceptance Criteria
- <Clear, testable criteria that define "done">
- ...

(For Cursor/Otto to fill in after working on the task)

3. Cursor worker prompt ‚Äì control/CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md
# Cursor Worker Instructions ‚Äì Queue Runner

You are working inside `residential_repo` on my local machine.
Your job is to execute tasks from the file-based task queue.

Follow this procedure exactly:

1. Look in `control/cursor_queue/` for files ending in `.md`.

2. For each file, find the line that starts with `status:` and identify tasks where:
   - `status: pending`

3. If there are no tasks with `status: pending`, respond with:
   `IDLE: No pending tasks in control/cursor_queue.`
   and stop.

4. Otherwise, pick the oldest pending task based on its `id` or filename (the lowest `YYYY-MM-DD_seq`).

5. Open that task file and:
   - Change `status: pending` to `status: in_progress`.
   - Do NOT modify the `Raw Input` section.
   - Use the `Parsed Instructions` and `Acceptance Criteria` sections as your source of truth.

6. Make all necessary code and documentation changes in the repo to satisfy the `Acceptance Criteria` for this task.

7. When you believe the task is fully completed:
   - Change `status: in_progress` to `status: done`.
   - Under `Implementation Notes`, add:
     - `- Changed files: <list of files you modified>`
     - `- Summary: <one or two sentences describing what you did>`

8. If you are unable to complete the task after reasonable attempts because something is missing, misconfigured, or unclear:
   - Change `status: in_progress` to `status: blocked`.
   - Under `Blocked Notes`, add:
     - What you tried (including any relevant file paths or commands)
     - Why it is blocked (e.g. missing API key, failing tests you cannot fix, ambiguity in requirements)
     - What information or change is needed to unblock the task

9. After updating the task file (to either `done` or `blocked`), repeat this entire procedure starting from step 1, until there are no more tasks with `status: pending`.

Never create or delete task files. Only update `status`, `Implementation Notes`, and `Blocked Notes` in existing tasks.
4. LLM Prompt ‚Äì Single input (voice/text ‚Üí one task)
Create prompts/intake_single_task_prompt.md (this is what your intake service sends to GPT/Claude along with the text):

You are a task-intake assistant for a developer automation system.

Your job:
- Take a single short human input (text or transcript from a voice note).
- Produce ONE well-structured task in a specific Markdown format.
- The task will be executed by Cursor (a coding assistant) inside a monorepo called `residential_repo`.

### Inputs

You will receive:

- `raw_input`: A short sentence or paragraph spoken or typed by Karl.

Examples of `raw_input`:
- "Catered: add allergen tags to recipes and show icons in the list view. High priority."
- "SMB site: make the floor plan cards clickable and route to detail pages for each plan."
- "Fix the finish selection bug in the prime-order app where the library sometimes doesn't show up."

app: <catered-by-me|smb_site|otto|personal|other>
priority: <low|normal|high|urgent>

created_by: karl

## Raw Input
<Paste the raw_input here verbatim.>

## Parsed Instructions
- <Bullet point 1 with a concrete, developer-facing instruction>
- <Bullet point 2>
- ...

## Acceptance Criteria
- <Bullet point 1 that defines "done" from Karl's perspective>
- <Bullet point 2>
- ...

## Implementation Notes
(For Cursor/Otto to fill in after working on the task)

## Blocked Notes

- What was tried:
- Why it is blocked:
- What is needed to proceed:
Rules
Infer app if Karl mentions "Catered", "SMB", "Otto", etc. Otherwise use personal or other.

Infer priority from words like "urgent", "high priority", "whenever", "later".

Make the Parsed Instructions as concrete and implementation-ready as possible without writing actual code.

Make Acceptance Criteria clear and testable.

## 5. LLM Prompt ‚Äì Meeting transcript ‚Üí many tasks

Create `prompts/intake_meeting_prompt.md`:

```md
You are a task-intake assistant for a developer automation system.

Your job:
- Read a long meeting transcript from Karl and collaborators.
- Identify all concrete, actionable tasks that relate to the codebase or dev tooling.
- For EACH such task, produce a separate Markdown document in a specific format.
- These tasks will be executed by Cursor inside a monorepo called `residential_repo`.

### Inputs

You will receive:

- `meeting_transcript`: a long text containing the full transcript of a meeting.

The transcript may include:
- high-level discussion
- decisions
- random chatter
- non-technical action items (wedding, errands, etc.)

### Your tasks

1. Read the transcript and extract only the **developer / automation / app-building** tasks. Ignore:
   - Personal errands
   - Non-software tasks (booking vendors, buying tools, etc.)

2. Group related comments into coherent tasks. If multiple people discuss one feature over several minutes, treat it as a single task.

3. For each task, infer:
   - `app` (catered-by-me, smb_site, otto, personal, or other)
   - `priority` (low, normal, high, urgent)
   - Clear developer-facing instructions and acceptance criteria.

### Outputs

Return a single response containing one or more Markdown documents concatenated, separated by a blank line.

Each document must follow this exact structure:

```md
# Task: <Short, imperative title>

id: <AUTO_GENERATED_ID>
status: pending
source: meeting
app: <catered-by-me|smb_site|otto|personal|other>
priority: <low|normal|high|urgent>
created_at: <AUTO_GENERATED_ISO8601_TIMESTAMP>
created_by: karl

## Raw Input
<Short excerpt(s) from the transcript that led to this task.>

## Parsed Instructions
- <Bullet point 1 with a concrete, developer-facing instruction>
- <Bullet point 2>
- ...

## Acceptance Criteria
- <Bullet point 1 that defines "done">
- <Bullet point 2>
- ...

## Implementation Notes
(For Cursor/Otto to fill in after working on the task)
- Changed files:
- Summary:

## Blocked Notes
(For Cursor to fill in ONLY if status becomes `blocked`)
- What was tried:
- Why it is blocked:
- What is needed to proceed:
Rules
For app, infer based on keywords in the Raw Input:

References to recipes, subscriptions, or "Catered" ‚Üí catered-by-me

References to Sugar Mountain, floor plans, SMB, homes ‚Üí smb_site

References to automation logic, Otto agent behavior, task pipeline itself ‚Üí otto

Miscellaneous dev tasks not tied to a specific app ‚Üí personal or other

Infer priority from the conversation:

"urgent", "needs to be done before launch" ‚Üí urgent

"high priority", "ASAP" ‚Üí high

"sometime later", "nice to have" ‚Üí low

Otherwise ‚Üí normal

Keep Raw Input short and only include the most relevant lines from the transcript, not the entire meeting.

Make Parsed Instructions detailed enough that a coding assistant knows what changes to make, but do not write actual code.

Make Acceptance Criteria clear, testable, and from Karl's perspective (what he would look at to confirm it's done).

Generate id values like 2025-12-01_00X_slug where X increments per task you emit. Use the current date and a simple slug based on the title. Uniqueness will be handled elsewhere.

## 6. Orchestrator skeleton ‚Äì `scripts/manage_cursor_pipeline.py`

This is a basic version with:

- Queue dir test + repair
- Intake health check hook (stub)
- Simple watcher loop for `pending` / `blocked`

You can let Cursor flesh this out further later.

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python
"""
manage_cursor_pipeline.py

Orchestrator for the Cursor task pipeline:
- Verifies repo and queue folder
- Checks basic config
- Optionally checks intake service
- Starts a simple watcher loop that reports pending/blocked tasks
"""

import os
import time
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Tuple

try:
    import requests  # optional, for intake health check
except ImportError:
    requests = None

# --- CONFIG ---

REPO_ROOT = Path(r"E:\My Drive\residential_repo")  # adjust as needed
CONTROL_DIR = REPO_ROOT / "control"
QUEUE_DIR = CONTROL_DIR / "cursor_queue"

INTAKE_HEALTH_URL = os.environ.get("INTAKE_HEALTH_URL", "http://localhost:5001/health")


# --- UTILITIES ---

def log(msg: str) -> None:
    print(msg, flush=True)


# --- CHECKS & REPAIRS ---

def check_repo_root() -> Tuple[bool, str]:
    if not REPO_ROOT.exists():
        return False, f"Repo root does not exist: {REPO_ROOT}"
    if not REPO_ROOT.is_dir():
        return False, f"Repo root is not a directory: {REPO_ROOT}"
    return True, f"Repo root OK: {REPO_ROOT}"


def check_and_repair_queue_dir() -> Tuple[bool, str]:
    if QUEUE_DIR.exists() and QUEUE_DIR.is_dir():
        return True, f"Queue directory OK: {QUEUE_DIR}"

    if QUEUE_DIR.exists() and not QUEUE_DIR.is_dir():
        return False, f"Queue path exists but is not a directory: {QUEUE_DIR}"

    try:
        QUEUE_DIR.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        return True, f"Queue directory created: {QUEUE_DIR}"
    except Exception as e:
        return False, f"Failed to create queue directory {QUEUE_DIR}: {e}"


def check_basic_env() -> Tuple[bool, str]:
    # Minimal check for now; extend as needed
    missing = []
    if "OPENAI_API_KEY" not in os.environ and "OTTO_API_KEY" not in os.environ:
        missing.append("OPENAI_API_KEY or OTTO_API_KEY")

    if missing:
        return False, f"Missing environment variables: {', '.join(missing)}"
    return True, "Basic environment variables OK"


def check_intake_health() -> Tuple[bool, str]:
    if not INTAKE_HEALTH_URL or not requests:
        return True, "Intake health check skipped (no URL or requests not installed)"

    try:
        resp = requests.get(INTAKE_HEALTH_URL, timeout=3)
        if resp.status_code == 200:
            return True, f"Intake service healthy at {INTAKE_HEALTH_URL}"
        return False, f"Intake service returned status {resp.status_code} at {INTAKE_HEALTH_URL}"
    except Exception as e:
        return False, f"Failed to reach intake service at {INTAKE_HEALTH_URL}: {e}"


# --- WATCHER ---

def count_tasks_by_status():
    counts = {"pending": 0, "in_progress": 0, "done": 0, "blocked": 0}
    for p in QUEUE_DIR.glob("*.md"):
        try:
            text = p.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
        except Exception:
            continue

        for status in ["pending", "in_progress", "done", "blocked"]:
            if f"status: {status}" in text:
                counts[status] += 1
                break
    return counts


def watcher_loop():
    last_counts = count_tasks_by_status()
    log(f"Watcher started. Pending={last_counts['pending']}, Blocked={last_counts['blocked']}")

    while True:
        time.sleep(60)  # adjust polling interval as needed
        counts = count_tasks_by_status()

        # New pending tasks
        if counts["pending"] > last_counts["pending"]:
            log(f"[INFO] New tasks added. Pending={counts['pending']} (was {last_counts['pending']})")

        # New blocked tasks
        if counts["blocked"] > last_counts["blocked"]:
            log(f"[WARN] New blocked tasks detected. Blocked={counts['blocked']} (was {last_counts['blocked']})")

        last_counts = counts


# --- MAIN ---

def main():
    print("=" * 40)
    print("  Cursor Task Pipeline ‚Äì Startup")
    print("=" * 40)

    ok, msg = check_repo_root()
    log(("[OK] " if ok else "[ERROR] ") + msg)
    if not ok:
        return

    ok, msg = check_and_repair_queue_dir()
    log(("[OK] " if ok else "[ERROR] ") + msg)
    if not ok:
        return

    ok, msg = check_basic_env()
    log(("[OK] " if ok else "[WARN] ") + msg)
    if not ok:
        log("[WARN] Environment incomplete. Intake service or LLM calls may fail.")

    ok, msg = check_intake_health()
    log(("[OK] " if ok else "[WARN] ") + msg)

    log("-" * 40)
    log("Pipeline is ready.")
    log(f"Queue directory: {QUEUE_DIR}")
    log("Start your intake service separately if not already running.")
    log("Run the Cursor Worker prompt inside Cursor to process tasks.")
    log("Watcher loop starting...")
    log("-" * 40)

    watcher_loop()


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

2. Create or overwrite `control/CONTROL_CURSOR_PIPELINE.md` with exactly this content:

```md
# CONTROL ‚Äì Cursor Task Pipeline

## Purpose

Turn messy human input (voice, text, meetings) into a structured queue of tasks that Cursor can execute without me manually copy/pasting between screens.

High-level flow:

1. Input:
   - Text (SMS / chat)
   - Voice notes / voicemail
   - Meeting recordings / long transcripts

2. Intake service:
   - Transcribes audio (if needed)
   - Uses an LLM to convert input ‚Üí standardized Markdown task files
   - Writes tasks into `control/cursor_queue/`

3. Cursor worker:
   - Uses a saved "Cursor Worker" prompt
   - Pulls tasks from the queue
   - Makes code changes
   - Marks tasks `done` or `blocked`

4. Watcher / Escalator:
   - Watches the queue for new `pending` or `blocked` tasks
   - Notifies me when there is work or when something is stuck
   - Optionally calls Otto to help triage blocked tasks


## Folder structure

```text
residential_repo/
  control/
    CONTROL_CURSOR_PIPELINE.md        <- this control doc
    CURSOR_TASK_TEMPLATE.md           <- template for a single task
    CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md           <- prompt for Cursor agent
    cursor_queue/                     <- one .md file per task
      2025-12-01_001_catered-filters.md
      2025-12-01_002_smb-floorplan-details.md
  prompts/
    intake_single_task_prompt.md      <- LLM prompt for single input
    intake_meeting_prompt.md          <- LLM prompt for meeting transcript
  scripts/
    manage_cursor_pipeline.py         <- orchestrator script (watcher + health checks)
Task lifecycle
Each task is a Markdown file in control/cursor_queue/ that follows CURSOR_TASK_TEMPLATE.md.

Statuses:

pending ‚Äì created by the intake service, waiting for Cursor

in_progress ‚Äì currently being worked on by Cursor

done ‚Äì successfully completed

blocked ‚Äì Cursor attempted work but could not finish; requires attention

All tools must only update status, Implementation Notes, and Blocked Notes. No tool is allowed to silently delete tasks.

Components
1. Intake service
Responsibilities:

Receive input from:

SMS / text

Voice notes / voicemail

Uploaded meeting recordings

Transcribe audio ‚Üí text (if needed)

Call an LLM with:

Single-input prompt (voice/text ‚Üí one task) or

Meeting prompt (long transcript ‚Üí many tasks)

Create .md files in control/cursor_queue/ using the template

Endpoints (example, to be implemented later):

POST /intake/single ‚Äì JSON { "source": "sms|voice|manual", "text": "..." }

POST /intake/meeting ‚Äì JSON { "source": "meeting", "transcript": "..." }

GET /health ‚Äì returns 200/OK if configured

Environment it needs:

OPENAI_API_KEY (or equivalent for Otto‚Äôs LLM calls)

Path to the repo root (e.g. REPO_ROOT)

2. Cursor Worker
Uses control/CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md inside Cursor.

Behavior:

Scan control/cursor_queue/ for .md files with status: pending

Take the oldest one, set in_progress

Do the work based on Parsed Instructions and Acceptance Criteria

Set status: done and fill out Implementation Notes

If it can‚Äôt finish:

Set status: blocked

Fill out Blocked Notes

Repeat until no pending remain

Finally respond: IDLE: No pending tasks in control/cursor_queue.

3. Watcher / Notifier
Script in scripts/manage_cursor_pipeline.py:

Validates:

Repo path exists

control/cursor_queue/ exists (creates if missing)

Environment keys are present (at least one of OPENAI_API_KEY or OTTO_API_KEY)

Intake service is reachable (/health) if configured

Starts a loop that:

Counts pending and blocked tasks

Logs or notifies when counts increase

Future: integrate OS notifications / SMS / Discord

How to use (human workflow)
Start the pipeline:

cd residential_repo
python scripts/manage_cursor_pipeline.py
Add tasks:

Talk to Frat (ChatGPT) ‚Üí copy spec into intake app

Text a number / drop a voice note into the intake app

Upload a meeting recording for parsing

Let the intake service write tasks into control/cursor_queue/.

When at the computer:

Open Cursor in residential_repo

Run the "Cursor Worker" prompt from CURSOR_WORKER_PROMPT.md

Watch it process tasks

If tasks are blocked:

Look at Blocked Notes in the task files

Optionally have Otto triage and create follow-up tasks

7. Create or overwrite `scripts/manage_cursor_pipeline.py` with this Python code:

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python
"""
manage_cursor_pipeline.py

Orchestrator for the Cursor task pipeline:
- Verifies repo and queue folder
- Checks basic config
- Optionally checks intake service
- Starts a simple watcher loop that reports pending/blocked tasks
"""

import os
import time
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Tuple

try:
    import requests  # optional, for intake health check
except ImportError:
    requests = None

# --- CONFIG ---

# Use the current working directory as repo root (assumes script is run from repo root)
REPO_ROOT = Path(os.getcwd())
CONTROL_DIR = REPO_ROOT / "control"
QUEUE_DIR = CONTROL_DIR / "cursor_queue"

# Intake health URL can be set via env var; otherwise skip check
INTAKE_HEALTH_URL = os.environ.get("INTAKE_HEALTH_URL", "")


# --- UTILITIES ---

def log(msg: str) -> None:
    print(msg, flush=True)


# --- CHECKS & REPAIRS ---

def check_repo_root() -> Tuple[bool, str]:
    if not REPO_ROOT.exists():
        return False, f"Repo root does not exist: {REPO_ROOT}"
    if not REPO_ROOT.is_dir():
        return False, f"Repo root is not a directory: {REPO_ROOT}"
    return True, f"Repo root OK: {REPO_ROOT}"


def check_and_repair_queue_dir() -> Tuple[bool, str]:
    if QUEUE_DIR.exists() and QUEUE_DIR.is_dir():
        return True, f"Queue directory OK: {QUEUE_DIR}"

    if QUEUE_DIR.exists() and not QUEUE_DIR.is_dir():
        return False, f"Queue path exists but is not a directory: {QUEUE_DIR}"

    try:
        QUEUE_DIR.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        return True, f"Queue directory created: {QUEUE_DIR}"
    except Exception as e:
        return False, f"Failed to create queue directory {QUEUE_DIR}: {e}"


def check_basic_env() -> Tuple[bool, str]:
    # Minimal check for now; extend as needed
    missing = []
    if "OPENAI_API_KEY" not in os.environ and "OTTO_API_KEY" not in os.environ:
        missing.append("OPENAI_API_KEY or OTTO_API_KEY")

    if missing:
        return False, f"Missing environment variables: {', '.join(missing)}"
    return True, "Basic environment variables OK"


def check_intake_health() -> Tuple[bool, str]:
    if not INTAKE_HEALTH_URL or not requests:
        return True, "Intake health check skipped (no URL configured or 'requests' not installed)"

    try:
        resp = requests.get(INTAKE_HEALTH_URL, timeout=3)
        if resp.status_code == 200:
            return True, f"Intake service healthy at {INTAKE_HEALTH_URL}"
        return False, f"Intake service returned status {resp.status_code} at {INTAKE_HEALTH_URL}"
    except Exception as e:
        return False, f"Failed to reach intake service at {INTAKE_HEALTH_URL}: {e}"


# --- WATCHER ---

def count_tasks_by_status():
    counts = {"pending": 0, "in_progress": 0, "done": 0, "blocked": 0}
    for p in QUEUE_DIR.glob("*.md"):
        try:
            text = p.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore")
        except Exception:
            continue

        for status in ["pending", "in_progress", "done", "blocked"]:
            if f"status: {status}" in text:
                counts[status] += 1
                break
    return counts


def watcher_loop():
    last_counts = count_tasks_by_status()
    log(f"Watcher started. Pending={last_counts['pending']}, Blocked={last_counts['blocked']}")

    while True:
        time.sleep(60)  # adjust polling interval as needed
        counts = count_tasks_by_status()

        # New pending tasks
        if counts["pending"] > last_counts["pending"]:
            log(f"[INFO] New tasks added. Pending={counts['pending']} (was {last_counts['pending']})")

        # New blocked tasks
        if counts["blocked"] > last_counts["blocked"]:
            log(f"[WARN] New blocked tasks detected. Blocked={counts['blocked']} (was {last_counts['blocked']})")

        last_counts = counts


# --- MAIN ---

def main():
    print("=" * 40)
    print("  Cursor Task Pipeline ‚Äì Startup")
    print("=" * 40)

    ok, msg = check_repo_root()
    log(("[OK] " if ok else "[ERROR] ") + msg)
    if not ok:
        return

    ok, msg = check_and_repair_queue_dir()
    log(("[OK] " if ok else "[ERROR] ") + msg)
    if not ok:
        return

    ok, msg = check_basic_env()
    log(("[OK] " if ok else "[WARN] ") + msg)
    if not ok:
        log("[WARN] Environment incomplete. Intake service or LLM calls may fail.")

    ok, msg = check_intake_health()
    log(("[OK] " if ok else "[WARN] ") + msg)

    log("-" * 40)
    log("Pipeline is ready.")
    log(f"Queue directory: {QUEUE_DIR}")
    log("Start your intake service separately if not already running.")
    log("Run the Cursor Worker prompt inside Cursor to process tasks.")
    log("Watcher loop starting...")
    log("-" * 40)

    watcher_loop()


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
When all files are created and saved, respond with a short summary of what you created and any TODOs (e.g., ‚Äúhook intake service to these prompts‚Äù).
Do NOT change any other existing files in the repo.

3Ô∏è‚É£ Data model + dashboard spec (for Cursor/Otto)
Minimal DB tables
households

id (uuid)

code (string, unique, e.g. ‚ÄúABCD1234‚Äù)

name (string, ‚ÄúThe Smith Family‚Äù)

email (optional, for sending invites)

notes

created_at

guests

id (uuid)

household_id (fk ‚Üí households.id)

first_name

last_name

email (optional)

phone (optional)

rsvp_status (yes | no | pending)

meal_choice (beef | chicken | veg | null)

dietary_restrictions (text or string[])

shuttle (boolean)

room_block (boolean)

song_request (text)

notes (text)

updated_at

events (just mirror wedding.events from config; seed this)

admins (if using custom auth; otherwise rely on Supabase auth roles)

RSVP flow (for dev spec)
Public route /rsvp/[code]:

Look up household by code.

Load guests for that household.

Render one card per guest with:

Toggle Yes/No

Meal select

Checkboxes for dietary restrictions

Optional phone, song request, notes.

Submit ‚Üí upsert guests, set rsvp_status, fire notification, show confirmation screen.

Admin dashboard /admin
Sections:

Overview

Counters:

Invited

Yes

No

Not responded

Mini-cards:

Beef / Chicken / Veg counts

needing shuttle
with special diets
Live activity

Table of recent RSVPs (ordered by updated_at desc).

Filter by date (‚ÄúToday‚Äù, ‚ÄúThis week‚Äù).

Guests

Search bar (name, code, email).

Table with inline edit or ‚Äúview details‚Äù drawer.

Export

Button: ‚ÄúDownload CSV for caterer‚Äù ‚Üí aggregated by guest, including meal, diet, notes.

Make it mobile-first: single-column, card-based layout, large tap targets. Perfect for your phone.
