You are building a production-quality Next.js wedding website for the domain britandkarl.com.

High level:
- Framework: Next.js (App Router, TypeScript)
- Hosting: Vercel
- Styling: TailwindCSS
- Auth + DB: Supabase
- Domain: britandkarl.com (DNS on Cloudflare, but we only care that Vercel serves the app)
- Config: We will have a file config/wedding_config.json as the single source of truth for wedding meta data.

Step 1 ‚Äì Project scaffold
- Initialize a new Next.js app in this repo (no example template, just a clean app).
- Add and configure:
  - TypeScript
  - TailwindCSS
  - ESLint + Prettier
- Create a folder structure:

  /app
    /(public)
      page.tsx
      layout.tsx
    /schedule
      page.tsx
    /travel
      page.tsx
    /stay
      page.tsx
    /faq
      page.tsx
    /rsvp
      [code]
        page.tsx
    /game
      page.tsx
    /admin
      layout.tsx
      page.tsx           (admin home)
      /rsvps
        page.tsx
      /tasks
        page.tsx

  /components
    (shared UI components)

  /lib
    (helpers, supabase client, config loader)

  /config
    wedding_config.json   (use the one that already exists or create it from the content in the editor)

- Ensure the app uses the App Router and the new file-based routing.

Step 2 ‚Äì Config loader
- In /lib/config.ts create a small module that:
  - Imports config/wedding_config.json
  - Exposes typed helpers like:
    - getBranding()
    - getWedding()
    - getVenue()
    - getLodging()
    - getTravel()
    - getFaq()
    - getGameConfig()
- Use TypeScript types so we get good IntelliSense.

Step 3 ‚Äì Branding and layout
- In app/layout.tsx:
  - Set global font to Inter for body and Playfair Display for headings (use next/font).
  - Use colors from config.branding:
    - primaryColor: #7D9BAE
    - secondaryColor: #2F3E56
    - accentColor: #27473B
    - softTone: #8DAA99
    - neutralBase: #D9D1C3
    - backgroundColor: #F5F6F4
    - metalAccent: #8A7759
    - candleGlow: #F8F5E8
  - Build a simple, elegant shell:
    - Top nav with logo text ‚ÄúKarl & Brit‚Äù
    - Links: Home, Schedule, Travel, Stay, FAQ, RSVP
    - Footer with date, venue name, and hashtag from config.

- Create shared components:
  - <PageSection> ‚Äì standard padding and max width
  - <Hero> ‚Äì for homepage hero using the tagline and colors
  - <Timeline> ‚Äì vertical or horizontal event timeline
  - <Card> ‚Äì generic card surface
  - <Button> ‚Äì primary, secondary, ghost styles driven by branding colors

Step 4 ‚Äì Public pages
Using config/wedding_config.json as the data source:

1) Home page (app/page.tsx)
   - Hero section:
     - Display couple displayNames, wedding date, tagline
     - Button: ‚ÄúView Schedule‚Äù (link to /schedule)
     - Button: ‚ÄúRSVP‚Äù (link to /rsvp without a code; show instructions)
   - Short ‚ÄúWelcome‚Äù / ‚ÄúOur Solstice‚Äù section with copy stub that we can edit later.
   - Feature strip with:
     - Venue card (name, city, link to travel page)
     - Date & time summary (key events)
     - Lodging highlight (primary hotel from config.lodging)

2) Schedule page (/schedule)
   - Use config.wedding.events and the venue locations.
   - Render a clean timeline with times, names, descriptions.
   - Make it responsive and easy to skim on a phone.

3) Travel page (/travel)
   - Airports section from config.travel.airports
   - Driving directions (from Spokane, from CDA)
   - Parking info
   - Shuttle notes and rideshare notes

4) Stay page (/stay)
   - Cards for each lodging option from config.lodging.hotels
   - Highlight primaryHotelId card
   - Show booking link, block name, block code (or ‚Äúcoming soon‚Äù if TBD).
   - Mention block cutoff date.

5) FAQ page (/faq)
   - Accordion list built from config.faq
   - Typography matches branding.

6) Game page (/game)
   - Implement a simple endless runner game called ‚ÄúSolstice Runner‚Äù
   - Use a <canvas> or simple div-based approach.
   - Controls:
     - Spacebar or tap to jump.
   - Obstacles scroll in from the right.
   - No backend; just client-side state.
   - Provide a ‚ÄúBack to home‚Äù link.

Step 5 ‚Äì Supabase integration
- Create a Supabase client module in /lib/supabaseClient.ts that reads:
  - NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL
  - NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY
- We will manage private service keys on the server side later if needed.

Database schema (SQL or migrations):

Table: households
- id: uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid()
- code: text unique not null
- name: text
- email: text
- notes: text
- created_at: timestamptz default now()

Table: guests
- id: uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid()
- household_id: uuid references households(id) on delete cascade
- first_name: text not null
- last_name: text not null
- email: text
- phone: text
- rsvp_status: text check (rsvp_status in ('yes','no','pending')) default 'pending'
- meal_choice: text
- dietary_restrictions: text
- shuttle: boolean default false
- room_block: boolean default false
- song_request: text
- notes: text
- updated_at: timestamptz default now()

Table: wedding_tasks
- id: uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid()
- title: text not null
- description: text
- status: text check (status in ('backlog','planning','in_progress','waiting','done')) default 'backlog'
- owner: text default 'Shared'
- category: text
- due_date: date
- priority: text check (priority in ('low','normal','high')) default 'normal'
- created_at: timestamptz default now()
- updated_at: timestamptz default now()
- completed_at: timestamptz

Table: admins
- id: uuid primary key default gen_random_uuid()
- user_id: uuid not null unique
- role: text check (role in ('owner','planner','viewer')) default 'owner'
- display_name: text

Step 6 ‚Äì Admin auth
- Use Supabase Auth with email/password or magic links.
- Implement a server-side helper that:
  - Checks the Supabase session
  - Verifies that the user has a matching row in admins.
- Protect all routes under /admin with this check.
- If user is not an admin, redirect to a simple ‚ÄúAdmin Login‚Äù screen.

Step 7 ‚Äì RSVP flow (public side)
- Route: /rsvp/[code]
  - Accept a URL param ‚Äúcode‚Äù.
  - Load the household by code from Supabase.
  - Load all guests in that household.
  - Render a card for each guest:
    - Toggle: attending yes/no
    - Select: meal_choice (values from config.rsvp.mealChoices)
    - Checkboxes or multi-select for dietary options (config.rsvp.dietaryOptions)
    - Optional fields: phone, song_request, notes
  - On submit:
    - Upsert each guest with updated fields and rsvp_status.
    - Update updated_at.
    - Show a confirmation screen summarizing their choices.

- Route: /rsvp (no code)
  - Explain that guests will receive a link with their RSVP code.
  - Provide a fallback ‚Äúcontact us‚Äù link if someone loses their link.

Step 8 ‚Äì Admin dashboard: RSVPs
- Route: /admin/rsvps
  - Stats at top:
    - Total invited (# of guests)
    - Total yes / no / pending
    - Meal breakdown counts by meal_choice
    - Number of guests needing shuttle, room_block, or special dietary notes
  - Table view:
    - List of guests with filters:
      - Search by name or household name.
      - Filter by rsvp_status, meal_choice.
  - Button: ‚ÄúExport CSV‚Äù which generates a CSV suitable for the caterer.

- Make this page mobile-first and very readable on a phone.

Step 9 ‚Äì Admin dashboard: Wedding Task Board (Kanban)
- Route: /admin/tasks
  - Implement a Kanban board with columns (swim lanes):
    - Backlog
    - Planning
    - In Progress
    - Waiting on Others
    - Done
  - Each column shows cards for tasks with corresponding status.
  - Each card shows:
    - Title
    - Owner (Karl, Brit, Shared, Vendor)
    - Category (catering, venue, decor, etc.)
    - Due date
    - Priority
  - Support drag-and-drop between columns; when a card is dragged to a new column, update status via Supabase.
  - Clicking (or tapping) a card opens a side drawer or modal with full details and the ability to edit fields.
  - Provide a simple ‚ÄúAdd Task‚Äù button that opens a form to create a new task.

- Make the Kanban board work nicely on mobile:
  - Columns horizontally scrollable
  - Cards vertically scrollable within each column
  - Big, tap-friendly hit targets.

Step 10 ‚Äì Admin home
- Route: /admin (index)
  - Simple landing with two main tiles:
    - ‚ÄúRSVP Dashboard‚Äù ‚Üí /admin/rsvps
    - ‚ÄúWedding Task Board‚Äù ‚Üí /admin/tasks
  - Also show high-level numbers:
    - Total RSVPs yes/no/pending
    - Total open tasks vs done tasks.

Step 11 ‚Äì Game page

  - Basic endless runner, obstacles, jump mechanic.

  - Describes the app

  - Gives basic Vercel deployment instructions
- Ensure that `npm run lint` and `npm run build` both pass with no errors.

1. ‚ÄúDo you actually need this much tech for a wedding?‚Äù
Devil‚Äôs advocate:

Weddings are one-off, high-stakes, low-reuse.

Joy, Zola, WithJoy, etc. handle RSVP, meal choices, reminders, room block info.

Trello/Notion/ClickUp handle wedding tasks way better than any v1 custom board.

Risk: You spend serious hours ‚Äúshipping a platform‚Äù and your time cost is way higher than just punting to a SaaS + nice Canva site.

Counterpoint in your favor:

2. Stack overkill & failure points

PWA + service worker: if misconfigured you can:

serve stale assets (‚ÄúWhy is this old version still showing up?‚Äù)

cause weird caching when you change routes close to the wedding.

Devil‚Äôs advocate conclusion:
For a wedding site, the riskiest parts (service workers, realtime, Kanban) are also the least essential.

Step 1 ‚Äì Project scaffold
- Initialize a clean Next.js App Router project in this repo with TypeScript.
- Add TailwindCSS and basic ESLint/Prettier setup.
- Create this structure:

  /app
    layout.tsx
    page.tsx                 (Home)

      page.tsx

Step 2 ‚Äì Config loader
- Put wedding_config.json in /config (use the JSON content already provided by the user).

  - Import the JSON.

    - getBranding()
    - getSite()

Step 5 ‚Äì Supabase integration (RSVP + admin auth)
- Create /lib/supabaseClient.ts:
  - Initialize Supabase client with NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL and NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY.
- Assume the following tables exist in Supabase:

  Table: households
  - id: uuid pk
  - code: text unique not null
  - name: text
  - email: text
  - notes: text
  - created_at: timestamptz default now()

  Table: guests
  - id: uuid pk
  - household_id: uuid references households(id) on delete cascade
  - first_name: text not null
  - last_name: text not null
  - email: text
  - phone: text
  - rsvp_status: text check (rsvp_status in ('yes','no','pending')) default 'pending'
  - meal_choice: text
  - dietary_restrictions: text
  - shuttle: boolean default false
  - room_block: boolean default false
  - song_request: text
  - notes: text
  - updated_at: timestamptz default now()

  Table: admins
  - id: uuid pk
  - user_id: uuid unique not null       (Supabase auth user id)
  - role: text check (role in ('owner','planner','viewer')) default 'owner'
  - display_name: text

- In /lib/auth.ts, add helpers:
  - getAdminSession() ‚Äì fetch Supabase session server-side.
  - requireAdmin() ‚Äì ensure the user has a matching row in admins; otherwise redirect to /admin/login.

- For now, you can stub an /admin/login page that uses Supabase email/password auth.

Step 6 ‚Äì RSVP flow

Route: /rsvp/[code]
- Server-side:
  - Read `code` from params.
  - Fetch household by code.
  - If not found, show a friendly error.
  - Fetch all guests in that household.
- UI:
  - Show household name, short instructions.
  - For each guest:
    - Radio: Attending? Yes/No
    - Select: meal_choice (options from config.rsvp.mealChoices)
    - Checkboxes or multiselect: dietary options from config.rsvp.dietaryOptions
    - Optional fields: phone, song_request, notes
  - Submit button:
    - Writes updated RSVP data to Supabase.
    - Sets rsvp_status = 'yes' or 'no' per guest.
  - On success, show a confirmation screen with their choices summarised.

Route: /rsvp
- Simple page explaining that guests will receive an RSVP link with their unique code.
- Provide fallback instructions (e.g., contact email from config.site.supportEmail).

Step 7 ‚Äì Admin dashboard (RSVP-focused only)

/admin (overview):
- Protected by requireAdmin().
- Show:
  - Total guests (count from guests table).
  - RSVP breakdown:
    - Yes / No / Pending counts.

  - Special counts:
    - # of guests with shuttle = true

    - # of guests with non-empty dietary_restrictions

- Use <StatCard> components for each metric.

/admin/rsvps:
- Protected by requireAdmin().

  - columns: name, household, rsvp_status, meal_choice, dietary_restrictions, shuttle, room_block, updated_at.

- Basic filters:
  - By status (All / Yes / No / Pending)
- Button ‚ÄúExport CSV‚Äù:
  - Calls an API route that queries guests + households and returns a CSV string.
  - Trigger a file download in the browser.

Make both admin pages very mobile-friendly, since the primary admin will often view them on a phone.

Thought for 34s
Short version: what you‚Äôre describing is totally buildable, and the sane path is not hacking KOTOR‚Äôs engine, it‚Äôs making a KOTOR-flavored, D&D-style text/retro game with:

D20-ish combat

Party management

Feats (not Fallout-style perk trees)

Skill-gated crafting

Eventually co-op if you want to go that far

Let me break it into options and then a concrete ‚Äúhere‚Äôs how we‚Äôd build it‚Äù plan.

1. What you‚Äôre actually asking for
Under all the Star Wars / ROM hack talk, I‚Äôm hearing:

You love KOTOR‚Äôs simple but crunchy D&D combat (attack rolls, AC, feats, etc.).

You want leveling + attributes + skills that actually matter for play.

You like feats, not giant perk trees ‚Äî small, meaningful choices, not 40-node tech trees.

You want crafting/weapon upgrades that unlock through skills/feats.

You‚Äôd love replayable content (different builds, different scenarios).

You‚Äôre fine if it‚Äôs text-based / Oregon Trail style as long as it feels like a game, not a spreadsheet.

Dream version: co-op, where you and someone else can run a party together.

That is 100% doable as an original game (no Star Wars IP, just ‚Äúinspired by‚Äù).

2. Three ways to approach it
Path A ‚Äì Mod an existing game (harder, more annoying)
You could:

Mod something like KOTOR / Neverwinter / etc.

Build new stories, classes, items with their toolsets.

But:

You‚Äôre trapped in someone else‚Äôs engine decisions.

It‚Äôs IP-messy if you ever share it beyond ‚Äúme and some friends‚Äù.

Toolchains are ancient and janky as hell.

Verdict: Interesting rabbit hole, but not the best use of your brainpower. Let‚Äôs not.

Path B ‚Äì Build your own ‚ÄúKOTOR in text form‚Äù (most realistic + fun)
This is where I‚Äôd steer you: a single-player (first), text/2D game with a clean rules engine.

Core ingredients:

Character system (D&D-ish)

Attributes: STR, DEX, CON, INT, WIS, CHA (or rename/simplify).

Derived stats: HP, Defense/AC, Initiative, Skill bonuses.

Skills: e.g. Mechanics, Persuade, Stealth, Medicine, Crafting, etc.

Feats: Power Attack, Rapid Shot, Duelist, ‚ÄúJedi-ish‚Äù analogs but generic.

Party

You always control 1‚Äì3 characters.

Out-of-combat: pick who leads, whose skills apply (like KOTOR).

In combat: round-based, you choose each party member‚Äôs action.

Combat

Turn-based.

D20 roll + attack bonus vs Defense/AC.

Damage = weapon dice + STR/DEX/etc.

Feats modify this: more attacks, crit range, special moves.

Crafting / upgrades

Items have slots: Crystal / Mod / Grip / Scope / etc.

Certain skills/feats unlock craft recipes (NOT perk tree gating).

Example:

Feat: ‚ÄúWeapon Tinkerer‚Äù: you can install Tier 1 mods.

Mechanics 5+: you can craft Tier 1‚Äì2 mods.

Mechanics 10+ and rare blueprint: Tier 3 mods.

Content structure

3. Concrete build plan (if we were actually going to build the thing)
Let‚Äôs imagine we‚Äôre doing Path B, with a Python/text MVP first. Here‚Äôs the stack + phases.

Stack for V1
Language: Python

Storage: JSON or a simple SQLite DB for:

Characters

Items

Feats

Encounters

Interface (V1): Command-line (you run python game.py)

Interface (V2): Tiny web app:

Backend: FastAPI or Flask

Frontend: simple HTML/JS (no need for React initially)

Phase 1 ‚Äì Define the rules (no code yet)
We‚Äôd create a mini ‚ÄúSYSTEM.md‚Äù:

Stats & leveling

Level 1‚Äì20.

Attribute points at creation, extra every X levels.

HP growth per level (by class, like D&D/KOTOR).

Classes / archetypes

Example:

Vanguard (frontline melee)

Marksman (ranged)

Mystic (caster / support)

Tech (skills + crafting beast)

Each class:

Hit die size

Skill points per level

Favored feats list

Feats

Each feat = name, description, prerequisites, mechanical effect.

No giant trees, but web of prerequisites.

Example:

Power Attack

Req: STR 13+

Effect: trade attack bonus for damage.

Weapon Modder

Req: Mechanics 5+

Effect: can craft tier 2 weapon mods.

Skills

Simple list: Mechanics, Stealth, Persuade, Medicine, Lore, Crafting.

Clear DC bands: Easy 10, Standard 15, Hard 20, etc.

Combat math

Attack = d20 + attack bonus.

Defense = 10 + armor + DEX + misc.

Crits on natural 20 (expand with feats).

Turn order = Initiative (DEX + d20).

Crafting

Recipes are just ‚Äúif player has skill X, feat Y, ingredient Z ‚Üí can craft mod Q‚Äù.

Mods define stat changes to weapons/armor.

Once that is nailed, code becomes ‚Äújust implementation‚Äù.

Phase 2 ‚Äì Build the core engine (no fancy UI)
Features to implement first:

Character entity

Data: name, class, level, XP, attributes, skills, feats, inventory.

Methods: attack roll, damage roll, skill check, level_up().

Enemy entity

Similar to character but simpler; many enemies can share templates.

Combat loop

Input: list of party members, list of enemies.

Output: who‚Äôs alive / dead, XP gained, loot.

Basic actions:

Attack

Use item

Special feat actions (once we add them)

Event system

Simple ‚Äústory nodes‚Äù:

Node: description text + options (A/B/C).

Option: leads to other node, triggers combat or skill checks, gives loot.

Saving/loading

Dump party + global flags to JSON.

Load from saved file to resume.

That‚Äôs enough to play ‚Äúgo into the cave, fight goblins, kill boss, get unique sword‚Äù.

Phase 3 ‚Äì Add the KOTOR-ish spice
Once it works:

Add feats that change playstyle

Dual Wielding vs. Two-Handed vs. Shield Tank.

Skill feats that open new options (crafting, dialogue unlocks, etc.).

Add crafting

Shops and workbenches:

‚ÄúYou find a workbench. What do you want to do?‚Äù

 Upgrade weapon
[ ] Break items into components
[ ] Craft mod (shows a list based on crafting skill/feats)

Add companions

Recruitable characters with:

Their own classes/feats.

Simple ‚Äúloyalty‚Äù flags or side quests.

Add mini-campaigns

Each campaign = a folder of JSON nodes, enemies, items.

Engine just loads whichever ‚Äúmodule‚Äù you choose.

This is where you get repeatable, KOTOR-feeling runs.

Phase 4 ‚Äì Co-op (if you want to go wild)
When you‚Äôre ready for co-op:

Turn the engine into a server:

Players connect via browser / simple client.

Server:

Stores party state.

Runs combat and dice rolls.

Broadcasts results to all players.

Easiest co-op style:

Two players each control different party members.

They vote on story choices, or one is ‚Äúparty leader‚Äù.

That‚Äôs more engineering, but completely feasible once the rules are solid.

SYSTEM.md
Game Rules Reference ‚Äì Draft v0.1
This document defines the foundational systems for the sci-fantasy RPG. It is not lore. It is the rulebook.

1. CORE ATTRIBUTES
Every character (player, companion, NPC) has these base attributes:

Strength (STR)
Physical force, melee damage, carry capability, recoil control.

Dexterity (DEX)
Precision, reflexes, ranged accuracy, stealth, dodging.

Constitution (CON)
Vitality, resilience, toxin resistance, HP scaling.

Intelligence (INT)
Scientific knowledge, hacking, mechanical reasoning, implant interfacing, crafting logic.

Willpower (WIL)
Mental fortitude, resistance to fear/honey psychosis, resistance to magic, Amber attunement potential.

Charisma (CHA)
Negotiation, leadership, intimidation, diplomacy, trade leverage.

2. DERIVED STATS
Health Points (HP)
= base by class + CON scaling.

Defense
= base armor + DEX bonus + specialized mods.

Initiative
= DEX + modifiers.

Accuracy Rating
= class base + DEX bonus + weapon quality.

Energy Shielding
Certain gear supplies regenerating protection vs energy damage; scales with INT or feats.

Honey Resistance
CON + WIL modifiers determine tolerance to negative honey effects.

3. PLAYABLE RACES
Four starting races. All familiar archetypes, re-skinned for a spacefaring setting.

Humans
Balanced stats, flexible feat options

Optimal diplomatic outcomes

Stonelocks (Dwarf-analog)
Industrial and hard-bodied; survivors of brutal mining systems.

+CON, +INT

High implant compatibility

Poor finesse: limited precision weapons and advanced aiming mods

Aeshura (Elf-analog)
Long-lived, neuro-sensitive, elegant technologists and explorers.

+DEX, +WIL

Special synergy feats for precision upgrades

Low implant tolerance under heavy load

Sylarin (Alien Variant)
Physiology partially symbiotic with native microbes; unusual sensory constructs, pheromone logic.

Bonus Honey tolerance

Unique synergistic aura interactions when paired with other races

Not compatible with some cybernetic mods

4. CLASSES
Simple core design: few classes, wide branching via feats, implants, and equipment.

Vanguard
Frontline bruiser and protector. STR/CON focused. Crowd control, melee threat, armor tanks.

Tech Specialist
INT-based gear-savant: crafting, hacking, unlocking advanced weapon slots, refining Honey, Amber devices.

Operative
DEX-focused ranged threats, snipers, scouts, assassins.

Diplomat
CHA-driven infiltrator, negotiator, faction manipulator, trade specialist. Bypasses fights, opens access, social unlocks.

Mystic Channeler (locked NPC class)
Reserved for the rare magic-capable companion. Not playable. Gains spell access only through event-based awakenings tied to Amber sites.

5. SKILLS
Mechanics ‚Äî crafting, mod forging, refining honey, opening chassis slots
Medicine ‚Äî surgery, poison neutralization, augment safety
Hacking ‚Äî penetration of security, AI bypass, system hijacks
Speech ‚Äî persuasion, coercion, negotiation
Survival ‚Äî tracking, environmental hazards, ambush detection
Piloting ‚Äî landing, evasive maneuvers, ship-linked actions
Amber Lore ‚Äî rare: deciphering ancient carvings, safely handling amber artifacts, staff resonance
Honey Distillation ‚Äî isolating strains, potency, purification, reagent mixing

6. FEATS (ARCHITECTURE)
Feats are rare and defining, not tiny numeric bonuses.
They unlock capabilities, not crumbs.

Examples (non-exhaustive placeholders):

Weapon Tinkerer I‚ÄìIII
Access to advanced slots on ballistic/energy weapons.

Lens Harmonist
Allows pairing of secondary component types not normally compatible.

Implant Integration
Expand total implants possible, or enable synergy passives.

Honey Catalyst
Unlocks planetary hybrid distillation outcomes.

Channel Attunement (racial + story locked)
Allows magic staff wielding ‚Äî only for chosen races, only after story rites.

7. LEVELING
Cap: Level 30.
Character power progression should feel deliberate, not inflated.

Combat strength grows slowly

Feats granted at fixed level intervals

Skills increase through level points

Attribute points at some levels

Weapon slot unlocks come from feats, race, story quests, and crafting milestones ‚Äî not level alone

8. WEAPON SYSTEM
Weapons belong to core families.
Each family uses a different internal upgrade anatomy and naming conventions.

8.1 Weapon Damage Families
Ballistic
Lead, flechette, mass accelerators, coil rifles.

Energy
Plasma, directed-light blades, pulse pistols, focused beam rifles.

Melee
Metal blades, plasma edged weapons, gravity hammers.

Vibro
High-frequency edge vibration; devastating melee impacts.

Explosive
Grenades, breaching charges, chemical payload launchers.

8.2 Slot Philosophy
Every weapon chassis has six upgrade slots, but the slot names and types depend on the weapon type.

Slots unlock through:

feats

crafting skills

story events

racial affinity

faction access

Honey-derived reagents

Amber attunement (rare slots)

8.3 Ballistic Weapons ‚Äì Slot Model
Chassis Core
Basic weapon architecture.

Barrel Assembly
Range, recoil, spread, penetration.

Trigger Matrix
Firing control, burst logic, rate of fire.

Stabilizer Rail
Aim assistance, recoil damping.

Magazine System
Ammo type, capacity, feed reliability.

Compensator Slot
Noise control, flash suppression, heat bleed.

8.4 Energy Weapons ‚Äì Slot Model
Crystal Core
Energy source, tuning potential, base damage curve.

Aux Crystal
Attunement, ion channeling, reaction shaping.

Lens Array
Focus, beam geometry, crit behavior.

Emitter Node
Discharge type, arc behaviors, burn depth.

Power Cell
Capacity, regen speed, overcharge threshold.

Conduit Network
Heat routing, stability, feedback regulation.

8.5 Melee Weapons ‚Äì Slot Model
Edge Medium
Material composition, sharpness behavior, Amber sensitivity.

Weight Module
Balance, force multiplier, strike momentum.

Guard Assembly
Hand defense, counter-impact mitigation, melee parry tools.

Core Spine
Structural integrity, force conduction, anti-shock matrix.

Grip Bonding
Control, finesse, special stance compatibility.

Impact Node
Optional: vibration, plasma edge, shock pulse on hit.

8.6 Vibro Weapons ‚Äì Slot Model
Vibration Core
Amplitude, frequency, stability.

Harmonic Coil
Resonance shaping, anti-armor modulation.

Heat Baffle
Overheat prevention, edge integrity.

Edge Socket
Material tuning: diamond lattices, alloy composites, Amber-trace infusion.

Grip Circuit
Control, stance, reactive parries.

Catalyst Matrix
Slot where rare Honey or Amber can be infused, tying vibration properties to supernatural forces.

8.7 Explosive Weapons ‚Äì Slot Model
Reaction Chamber
Payload intensity and stability.

Fuse Logic
Trigger type, delay, proximity behavior.

Payload Casing
Blast pattern, fragmentation type.

Delivery Tube
Projectile stability, range, arc.

Catalytic Insert
Chemical booster slot (Honey distillates).

Safeguard Chip
Prevents self-harm, toggles friendly-fire constraints.

9. HONEY SYSTEM
Honey is universal currency, theology, chemistry, addiction, and magic reagent.

9.1 Base Types (Planet-Locked)
Each inhabited world produces one fundamental Honey strain based on its flora.

Examples:

Ironflower Honey ‚Üí Strength buff

Haze Bloom Honey ‚Üí Perceptual distortion, mild psionic visions

Nightroot Honey ‚Üí Sedation, toxin resistance, anesthetic value

Amaranth Nectar Honey ‚Üí Vitality, regenerative properties

Planets define base structure.

9.2 Hybrid Honey (Mixed)
Alchemic fusion of two or more strains produces new, unstable effects:

double-buff

buff + penalty

corrupted variants

catalysts for weapon component upgrades

pathways to convert Honey ‚Üí Amber crystals

Only Tech Specialists with Honey Distillation feats can produce stable hybrids.

9.3 Honey & Implants
Some reagents must be metabolized before high-end cybernetics are tolerated.
They become:

neural soothe

anti-rejection substrate

booster compounds for template bonding

10. AMBER SYSTEM
Amber = crystallized metaphysical essence produced only when Honey saturates in exact cosmic conditions.

Functions:

Required for ANY true magic

Used in magical staff cores

Required to awaken the Channel feat

Rare enchantment slot for weapons

Non-replicable by synthetic methods

Amber is sacred, terrifying, and unstable in the wrong hands.

11. MAGIC CHANNELING
Magic cannot be cast by anyone without:

Unlocked Channel Attunement feat

Staff with Amber core

Location/event-based ritual triggers

Magic Companion unlocks spells only through:

shrines

ruins

planetary alignments

remnants of past civilizations

Spells fall into:

Burst (impact)

Support (buff/heal/shield)

Domain (battlefield control)

12. EVENT-GATED MAGIC PROGRESSION
Magic progression ignores levels.
It obeys story.

When certain Amber shrines, ruins, or rituals are encountered:

spells unlock

purity increases

new Honey catalysts become usable

deeper attunements possible

Magic remains frightening, rare, and never common in combat.

13. IMPLANTS & SYNERGY
Implants:

boost attributes

unlock chassis slots

change damage types

add passive effects

open unique feats

Costs/risk:

some reduce Honey tolerance

some cause long-term maladies

some block magical resonance

Cross-Character Synergy:
Certain implants or racial traits generate ambient effects when specific teammates are present.

Examples:

Dwarf + Elf ‚Üí ranged accuracy & recoil stability

Sylarin + Human ‚Üí social aura or honey resistance boost

Mystic Companion + Tech Specialist ‚Üí synthetic Amber disrupts real Amber fields, creating unpredictable combat bonuses or malfunctions

Party composition matters.

14. COMPANION STRUCTURE
max party: 3‚Äì4 active

companions have personal feat trees

races create different upgrade pathways

relationships, faction ties, background lore unlock special craftsmanship and hidden slot types

Magic companion eventually becomes the keystone of late-game synergy.

15. LEVEL CAP: 30
Power curve:

slow, meaningful growth

feats every fixed number of levels

skill points every level

attribute at milestones only

late-game builds feel earned, not granted

Final party: lvl 30 facing lvl 50 nightmare boss with perfect weapon mastery, Amber rites completed, and synergy fully realized.

SYSTEM v0.1 COMPLETE

Races, classes, feats, quests, crafting, magic, Honey, Amber, weapons, synergy ‚Äî all grounded.

Or if you want, I can immediately:

Whatever direction you pick next, this rulebook is now the foundation.

1. WEAPON ARCHITECTURE (Shape ‚Üí Damage Type)

Weapon Shape ‚Üí Damage Family ‚Üí Slot Model & Cost Structures

medicine

3. STANDARD CURRENCY
Yes: a universal ‚Äúcredit‚Äù currency remains necessary.

Rational tiering:

Honey ‚Üí alchemy, implants, augment rarity, diplomacy with special factions

Amber ‚Üí instanced only. Magic-level stuff. Often plot-sealed.

Amber should be so rare that the player recognizes it as existential wealth ‚Äî NOT a shopping item.

4. ARMOR SYSTEMS & CLASS RESTRICTIONS
Armor needs to mirror KOTOR‚Äôs logic:

Certain classes simply CANNOT wear certain armor tiers without Feats.

Certain races reject certain armor tech altogether.

We formalize armor too as shape first, subtype second:

Armor Category ‚Üí Material Origin/Type ‚Üí Resistances & Slot System
ARMOR CATEGORIES
Light Armor
Fabric composites, tactical skins, micro-fiber synth weave.
High mobility.
Low resistances.

Medium Armor
Ceramic plates, kinetic dampeners, smart textiles.
Balanced resistances, moderate durability, some energy shielding.

Heavy Armor
Metallic lamination, powered chassis, hydraulic reinforcements.
High ballistic resistance, high kinetic threshold.
Poor DEX synergy.

Exo-Armor
Late-tier suits with cybernetic assist modules.
High mass, high cost, often locked behind implants and Tech Specialist feats.

Amber-Bound Armor
Ultra rare. Channels Honey or Amber resonance.
Not necessarily heavy or light ‚Äî they bend rules.

These should be extremely limited, story-gated, and only truly useful with synergy feats and Amber rites.

ARMOR SLOTS
Characters have:

Helmet (or Visor)

Chest Harness

Arms/Wrist Plate

Legs Greaves

Utility Belt (capacity, ammo, stims)

Shield Generator (energy barrier system)

Implant Slots (internal, not ‚Äúworn‚Äù)

Neural

Skeletal

Organ

Muscle

Optical

Cyber-link ports

Implants are separate from armor, but can affect armor behavior.

Example:

Dwarf-analog can mount heavier exoskeleton components

Elf-analog cannot sustain them, but can use ultra-advanced neural targeting visors instead

Armor sets produce set bonuses, but set bonuses are NOT dominant: synergy is king.

5. CLASS & FACTION ARMOR LOCKS

ARTIFICIAL (Implants)

Examples:

Organ implant + DEX-enhancing ocular rig on another character = shared aim aura

Skeletal reinforcement + kinetic shield generator = shared shock-mitigation pulse

Implants must feel like:

cyber-biology learned to copy some secrets of Honey

but can never fully reach Amber

7. ARMOR RESISTANCE TYPES
Armor will resist damage families differently:

Ballistic Resistance

Energy Shielding

Kinetic/Impact Dampening

Ion/EMP Hardening

Chemical Baffling

Cryo insulation

Honey Corrosion Resistance

Amber Resonance Stability

Heavy armor excels at:

Ballistic and kinetic
Suffers in:

Energy

Chemical penetration

Ion

Light armor excels at:

Stealth, DEX scaling, honey tolerance
Suffers in:

raw mitigation

Mystic-compatible armor:

must avoid blocking Amber flow

too much metal disrupts spells

too much cybernetic complexity dampens field sensitivity

8. PARTY KIT OPTIMIZATION IS NOW AN INTENTIONAL PUZZLE
What you said nails the soul of the game:

‚ÄúIt should be difficult, rewarding, and strategic to create a good kit.‚Äù

Beautiful.

This is NOT a game where:

you pick Strong Guy and Strong Guy wins

full plate + biggest gun trivializes encounters

This is a game where synergy of:

armor slot layout

implants

race traits

Honey reagents

Amber resonance

weapon chassis

magic anomalies

companion composition

creates mastery.

This means no single character is ever the ‚Äúoptimal build.‚Äù
The party is the build.

Exactly like Kreia ‚Üí Exile bonding, but extended to:

races

implants

Honey catalysts

armor fields

SYSTEM.md (v0.2 ‚Äî Core Rules Reference)
Last updated: by ChatGPT with user collaboration

This document defines the underlying rules, itemization, resource systems, combat interactions, and progression scaffolding for the as-yet-unnamed RPG.

It is not story, lore, or flavor text.
It is the spine the game engine is built on.

1. ATTRIBUTES
Every character has six core attributes:

Strength (STR)
Melee damage, carry load, recoil control, blunt mitigation.

Dexterity (DEX)
Accuracy, initiative, stealth, ranged precision, evasion.

Constitution (CON)
HP scaling, endurance, toxin resistance, Honey tolerance.

Intelligence (INT)
Crafting, hacking, weapon slot unlocking, Honey distillation, implant interfacing.

Willpower (WIL)
Mental defense, Amber resonance potential, Honey psychosis resistance.

Charisma (CHA)
Speech checks, diplomacy, trade leverage, faction trust.

2. DERIVED STATS
HP = Class base + CON scaling
Defense = Armor rating + DEX mods
Initiative = DEX + equipment/passives
Accuracy = DEX + weapon chassis rating
Energy Shielding = gear-based tech layer
Honey Resistance = CON + WIL + gear/implants
Amber Stability = WIL + race bonuses

3. PLAYABLE RACES
Human
Balanced attribute spread

Strong Speech outcomes

Most flexible feat options

Stonelock (Dwarf-Analog)
+CON, +INT

Best implant capacity

Limited precision/aiming systems

Aeshura (Elf-Analog)
+DEX, +WIL

Best precision mods

Poor tolerance for heavy cybernetics

Sylarin (Alien Variant)
Unique microbial symbiosis

Exceptional Honey tolerance

Cannot accept certain implants

4. CLASSES
Vanguard
STR/CON bruiser. Armor tank. Crowd control.

Tech Specialist
INT-focused mastercraft class.
Unlocks advanced weapon slots, hybrid Honey recipes, implant approvals.

Operative
DEX-focused marksman, scout, assassin.
Critical shots, stealth, reconnaissance.

Diplomat
CHA-based social manipulator, negotiator, faction broker.
Unlocks access, trade, bypass routes.

Mystic Channeler (NPC only)
Magic companion archetype.
Magic awakened via Amber rites and story milestones.
Not playable.

5. SKILLS
Mechanics

Medicine

Hacking

Speech

Survival

Piloting

Amber Lore

Honey Distillation

Skills feed crafting, slot unlocking, negotiations, weapon growth, and access to synergy perks.

6. FEATS (STRUCTURE)
Feats unlock capability, not micro-buffs.

Examples:

Weapon Tinkerer (I‚ÄìIII) ‚Üí unlock Tier 2‚Äì4 upgrade slots

Implant Integration ‚Üí more implant capacity

Honey Catalyst ‚Üí stable hybridization

Armor Specialist: Medium/Heavy/Exo

Channel Attunement ‚Üí staff magic (locked to specific races, story rites)

Feats must matter in combat, crafting, faction outcomes, or synergy.

7. LEVELING
Level Cap: 30

Guiding principles:

Slow power curve

Feats are milestone unlocks

Skills improve each level

Attributes awarded only at select plateaus

Slot unlocks depend on feats, implants, story, and race‚Äînot level alone

8. WEAPON SYSTEM
A) Weapon Shapes
Primary structural category for chassis design.

Ranged

Bladed Staves

Explosive

Grenades

Remote Charges

Satchel Breakers

Weapon Shapes determine the slot architecture.

B) Damage Families
Any Shape may be built under one of these:

Ballistic

Energy

Hybrid Honey-Bond

Vibro

Chemical

Magnetic/EMP

Cryonic

This decides the TYPE of mods and materials inside each slot, not the slot names themselves.

9. ARMOR SYSTEM
Armor Categories
Light ‚Äî tactical fabrics, mobility, stealth
Medium ‚Äî plates, dampeners, composite shields
Heavy ‚Äî metal, power assist, bulk mitigation
Exo ‚Äî cybernetic chassis, hydraulic frames
Amber-Bound ‚Äî ritual armor, resonance-dependent

Neural

Light ‚Üí Heavy, Exo allowed with feats

Light default

Light default

Medium with feats

Heavy never

Chemical

EMP/Ion

Amber Field Stability

Armor shape + material defines resistances and drawbacks.

10. IMPLANTS
Implants grant power at a cost.

Effects:

attribute bonuses

slot unlocking

new damage channels

shared synergy auras

resistances

unique feat prerequisites

Downsides:

Honey tolerance reduction

Amber instability

long-term physiological risk

unlock restrictions by class and race

Implants also allow cross-character resonance buffs:

aim assist

honey immunity field

shared regeneration

neural synchronization

battlefield stability pulses

Party composition becomes a mechanical build puzzle.

11. HONEY SYSTEM
20 Base Strains (Planet-Locked)
Each strain has:

core trait

secondary quirk

utility class

base reagent profile

Honey categories:

Buffing

Healing

Catalytic (unlocking slots, forging materials)

Metabolic (affects implants & cybernetic grafting)

Toxin variants

Rare Mutation strains

Hybridization
2‚Äì4 strain combinations produce unique effects.

The total pool of possible hybrids far exceeds what the game needs to define.

Only Tech Specialists with correct feats can produce STABLE hybrids.

Honey Uses
medical healing

alchemy

crafting catalysts

slot unlock materials

currency alternative

faction negotiations

Amber crystal refinement precursor

Honey is the most versatile substance in the universe.

12. AMBER SYSTEM
Amber is crystallized metaphysical essence, not scientifically reproducible and not technically ‚Äúenergy.‚Äù
Reacts violently to synthetic analogs.

Amber enables:

magic via staff focus

late-tier weapon slots

armor resonance

shrine rituals

anti-machine disruption fields

Amber must be found, earned, or ritually refined from Honey.
Never sold casually.

13. MAGIC UNLOCKING
Magic is a story-based phenomenon, not a skill progression.

Only:

The Mystic Companion

Specific race with proper feat

Staff with Amber core

Ritual-event unlock state

Magic unlocks are tied to shrines, ruins, cosmic alignments, NOT XP level.

Spell categories:

Burst

Support

Domain

Magic is rare enough to feel biblical every time it‚Äôs used.

14. RESOURCES & ECONOMY
Credits
Standard universal money. Used for:

gear

travel

supplies

minor weapon mods

Honey
Alchemy, crafting, medicine, mutation, Amber precursor.

Amber
Staff cores, high-end rituals, existential rarity.

15. PARTY SYNERGY ARCHITECTURE
This game is NOT about the single optimal build.
It is about crafting a party that interlocks.

Synergies emerge from:

racial pairing

implant resonance

armor resonance

Honey strain combinations

Amber ritual bonuses

weapon chassis alignment

class skill coverage

diplomacy routes

The ‚Äúmeta‚Äù is finding combinations the universe itself didn‚Äôt expect.

END SYSTEM.md v0.2
DEVIL‚ÄôS ADVOCATE ANALYSIS
Here‚Äôs a critical pass on what we‚Äôve built.

Strengths:
‚úî Deep interlocking systems
Weapons, Honey, Amber, armor, implants, race, class ‚Äî all cross-feed each other. This guarantees replayability and theorycrafting.

‚úî Magic is rare, earned, mythic
That makes late-campaign unlocks feel monumental.

‚úî Honey as the central alchemy system
This gives the game a unique flavor ‚Äî no one has ever built mechanics around apiculture as a metaphysical substrate.

‚úî Weapon shapes before damage models
Clean, logical, extensible.

‚úî Party synergy replaces min-maxing
Players are pushed to think like a commander, not just a stat mathematician.

Potential Weak Spots (Design Risks)
‚ùó Complexity Barrier
The system borders on ‚Äútoo interesting to fail‚Äù but also ‚Äútoo dense to pick up casually.‚Äù
UI needs to do a LOT of heavy lifting:

tooltips

recipe previews

mod slot highlighting

synergy diagrams

If we don‚Äôt make it readable, casual players will bounce.

‚ùó Honey Hybrid Explosion
If we allow 2, 3, and 4-strain combinations, the potential space of effects becomes massive.
We MUST cap the number of meaningful hybrids and make the rest useless, unstable, or dangerous.

‚ùó Magic Companion Danger
The magic companion could become:

too weak (if rare spells are underpowered)

too dominant (if bursts trivialize encounters)

Magic must be more strategic than destructive ‚Äî support-focused, battlefield control, non-damage miracles.

‚ùó Armor Restrictions Must Never Feel Arbitrary
Players hate ‚ÄúYou just can‚Äôt‚Äù without explanation.

Every restriction must be:

biological

logical

lore-supported

‚ùó Synergy Must Be Visible
If the system is deep, but hidden, players will miss it.

We‚Äôll need:

synergy popups

aura visual hints

buff stacking logs

Otherwise, they won‚Äôt know what to chase.

Most Important Missing Pieces (Next Round)
1. Combat Math
Hit rolls, crit behavior, damage reductions, armor mitigation formulas.

2. Turn Flow
Initiative, actions, reaction abilities, ambush conditions.

3. AI Behavior Grid
Enemy roles, threat assessments, swarm logic, area control.

4. Crafting Recipes
We don‚Äôt need 200, but 20 meaningful ones.

5. Honey Strain Index
Name list + base effects.

6. Weapon Stat Baselines
Start values for starter pistol, rifle, sword, etc.

7. Progression Curve
XP per level, milestone feats, skill point counts.

8. Tech Tree UI Concepts
We need clarity for:

Weapon mod screens

Honey alchemy bench

Implant terminal

Amber shrine rituals

Role
Closest comparison:

Field biologist

Hunter-herbalist

Honey gatherer

Planetary mechanic

They don‚Äôt study Amber as relics (like Reclaimers do), and they don‚Äôt fabricate or distill Honey with machines (like Tech Specialists do).
They know the organisms, terrain, breed cycles, threats, symbiosis chains, extinction events, and how ecosystems converse with Amber at the root level.

They are wilderness in human (or non-human) form.

Core Competencies
1. Environmental knowledge
Identify viable Honey sources on any world

Predict which flora and fauna produce what strains

Understand inter-species dependencies

Recognize contamination signals

Detect Honey rot, parasitic fungus, crystalline Amber infestation

2. Living world manipulation
Attempt natural hybridization without machines

Use terrain as cover, trap, or even weapon

Control the ecological state of a battlefield
(chilled fog, thick pollen clouds, pheromone trails)

3. Harvesting modules
Extract rare glands, pollens, plant hearts

Create bio-stimulants

Gather Amber seeds embedded in root systems

Preserve microflora to culture Honey off-world

4. Honey visions
They are uniquely susceptible to Amber psycho-visions when exposed to honey at over-concentrated purity.

NOT magic.
Not spellcasting.

But prophetic ecosystem memory ‚Äî like the biosphere imprinting its trauma and history through the Pioneer‚Äôs brain.

These vision events act as:

story revelations

precursor to magic awakenings for the companion

source of new Honey hybrids

planetary map unlocks

rituals to cleanse corrupted Amber zones

5. Inter-species diplomacy
When encountering non-civilized species:

Pioneers get unique dialogue

identify fauna intentions

pacify, bond, or control wildlife

unlock rare organic catalysts

Humans, Stonelocks, or industrialized races CANNOT fully replace the Pioneer‚Äôs ecological intuition.

## Summary

I read the conversation transcript in symbioz/chat from first run with frat.txt. It outlines a text-based RPG inspired by Knights of the Old Republic with:

- 8 playable classes (+ NPC Channeler)

## Devil's Advocate Summary Created

I've created symbioz/DEVILS_ADVOCATE_SUMMARY.md with critical concerns:

### Top concerns
1. No defined gameplay loop ‚Äî systems are described, but not how the game plays
2. Text-based games are niche ‚Äî small audience, may need visuals
3. Scope explosion ‚Äî 10 races √ó 8 classes √ó complex systems = massive project
4. Combat system undefined ‚Äî core mechanic is unclear
5. No story/narrative system ‚Äî what drives players forward?
6. Co-op/multiplayer undefined ‚Äî single-player vs multiplayer changes everything

### Recommendations
- Define the core gameplay loop first
- Design the combat system before building systems
- Start with an MVP (3 races, 4 classes, basic systems)
- Build a tiny prototype to test if it's fun
- Validate the text-based format with playtesters

The full document includes 21 concerns, recommendations, and success criteria.

## Step 0 ‚Äì Understand the existing context

1. Locate and read:
   - `symbioz/chat from first run with frat.txt` (or similar conversation log)
   - `symbioz/DEVILS_ADVOCATE_SUMMARY.md` (or the equivalent file in the repo)

## Step 1 ‚Äì Design docs (text only, no code yet)

Create a new folder: `symbioz/design/`

Inside it, create three markdown files:

### 1. `GAMEPLAY_LOOP.md`
Define the **moment-to-moment gameplay loop** for a **single-player, text-based CLI MVP**, not the full future game.

Constrain yourself to a simple loop like:
- Hub ‚Üí Choose mission ‚Üí Narrative node ‚Üí (skill check or combat) ‚Üí Outcome ‚Üí Loot/XP ‚Üí Back to hub.

Include:
- A clear description of the HUB: what the player can do there (e.g., talk, shop, rest, take missions).
- The structure of a MISSION: intro text, choices, checks, combat, rewards.
- Runtime goals: what 20‚Äì40 minutes of play should feel like.
- Explicit notes about what is **deliberately deferred** to future phases (e.g., co-op, ship combat, full Amber magic, etc.).

### 2. `COMBAT_SYSTEM.md`
Define a **simple, D20-style, turn-based combat system** for a party of up to 3 characters vs 1‚Äì4 enemies.

Include:
- Turn order (initiative formula).
- Action economy per turn (e.g., 1 main action: Attack / Ability / Use Item / Defend).
- Attack roll formula (e.g., `d20 + AttackBonus vs Defense`).
- Damage calculation (weapon base + STR/DEX mods ‚àí armor).
- Minimal set of status effects (e.g., Staggered, Guarded, Bleeding).
- How Honey (in the MVP) fits into combat (if at all), in a **simple** way.
- Explicit simplifications that keep it easy to implement and test in a CLI.

### 3. `MVP_SCOPE.md`
Lock in the **MVP constraints**. Be explicit and ruthless.

For the MVP CLI prototype, constrain to:
- **Races**: exactly 3 (e.g., Human, Stonelock, Aeshura).
- **Classes**: exactly 4 (e.g., Vanguard, Operative, Tech Specialist, Pioneer).
- **Honey**: exactly 5 base strains, no complex multi-strain hybrids yet.
- **Weapons**: exactly 2 shapes (Pistol and Sword), each with a reduced slot model (e.g., 3 meaningful slots for MVP).
- **Armor**: only Light and Medium classes.
- **Magic/Amber**: NOT implemented in MVP (no Channeler mechanics yet).
- **Mode**: Single-player only, no multiplayer/co-op.
- **Content**: 1 hub location, 2‚Äì3 simple missions, a handful of enemy types.

Also:
- List the ‚ÄúPhase 2+‚Äù systems (full 10 races, 8 classes, huge Honey matrix, Amber magic, implants complexity, co-op, etc.) as **explicitly deferred** items so we don‚Äôt forget them, but don‚Äôt try to design them here.

---

## Step 2 ‚Äì Build a tiny CLI prototype

Create a new app folder: `apps/symbioz_cli/`

Target: a **Python CLI** (unless the repo strongly suggests another language; if so, explain your choice in comments).

Structure (suggested):

- `apps/symbioz_cli/main.py`
  - Entry point. Runs a text-based menu loop:
    - Show hub options
    - Let the player choose a mission
    - Run through narrative ‚Üí encounter ‚Üí outcome
    - Return to hub

- `apps/symbioz_cli/models/`
  - `character.py` ‚Äì Character data: name, race, class, attributes, HP, XP, level, inventory.
  - `race.py` ‚Äì Data model for the 3 MVP races.
  - `clazz.py` ‚Äì Data model for the 4 MVP classes.
  - `weapon.py` ‚Äì Pistol and Sword models with simplified slot logic.
  - `armor.py` ‚Äì Light and Medium armor.
  - `enemy.py` ‚Äì Basic enemy model.

- `apps/symbioz_cli/systems/`
  - `combat.py` ‚Äì Implements the rules from `COMBAT_SYSTEM.md`.
  - `skill_checks.py` ‚Äì Very simple skill/attribute checks for narrative nodes.
  - `progression.py` ‚Äì XP and level-up logic (keep simple but visible).
  - `hub.py` ‚Äì Logic for the hub menu, visiting shop, resting, picking missions.

- `apps/symbioz_cli/data/`
  - JSON or YAML files for:
    - Races
    - Classes
    - Weapons
    - Armor
    - Honey strains (5)
    - A couple of small missions with simple branching text.

**Goals for this prototype:**
- The player can:
  - Create a character (pick 1 of 3 races, 1 of 4 classes).
  - See initial stats and starting gear.
  - Visit a basic hub menu.
  - Choose at least 1 mission.
  - Encounter a fight using the `COMBAT_SYSTEM.md` rules.
  - Gain XP, level up once, and see a visible improvement (e.g., +Attack or +Max HP or a small perk).

Avoid:
- Networking
- Databases
- Authentication
- Any web UI
- Any large asset pipelines

This is **just a CLI game**, functioning as a design and fun-proving sandbox.

---

## Step 3 ‚Äì Devil‚Äôs Advocate review of the MVP

1. Create `symbioz/DEVILS_ADVOCATE_MVP_ROUND2.md`.

     - too simple,
     - too random,
     - too grindy,
     - or about right for this stage?
   - Are 3 races + 4 classes enough to show off the potential, or does it feel flat?
   - Is Honey present in a way that feels interesting, or is it just an extra healing potion?
   - What parts feel most ‚Äúalive‚Äù and what feels like dead weight?

3. Propose:
   - The **top 3** changes to make the CLI prototype more engaging for a 30‚Äì60 minute session.
   - A minimal next step for expanding *either*:
     - another race,
     - another class,
     - a first bit of Amber/magic,
     - or a slightly richer Honey interaction.

Be blunt and practical. Keep everything grounded in making a small, fun, testable game loop instead of building the entire dream system at once.

üßÇ NOW FOR THE FUN PART: CRITICAL NOTES
1. Combat is a little too RNG heavy
4+ misses in a row will get old fast.

Early D&D-based systems always run into this problem.

With:

low-level Attack bonuses

small damage ranges

single-enemy fights

‚Ä¶it means rounds drag.

Quick fix (and I‚Äôd 100% instruct Otto to do this)
Implement Graze hits:

If your attack roll is within 3 points of the enemy‚Äôs Defense, deal half damage instead of missing.

This gives:

feedback every turn

shorter fights

less ‚Äúwhiff fatigue‚Äù

more sense of progress

Result:
Your pistol peppering a scavenger feels gritty instead of pointless.

2. First Aid healing the enemy is hilarious‚Ä¶ but too punishing
This might‚Äôve been a miswired target,
but I actually love the chaos energy of it.

Still:

I‚Äôd make it self-cast only (for MVP)

Later, Pioneers can have wild ‚Äútransfer wound‚Äù abilities or ‚Äútriage on enemies‚Äù but not yet

For now:
Force First Aid to always target self.
No menu required.

We want:

fewer clicks

less confusion

more confidence

3. Bleed is great mechanic‚Ä¶but small numbers stall combat
1 damage per turn is perfect for MVP,
but we need better combat pacing.

Suggest:

Enemy HP 10‚Äì12 instead of 15 for MVP grunts

Bleed scaling via DEX or weapon slot bonus later

Right now, it‚Äôs ‚Äúslow inevitability‚Äù ‚Äî which isn‚Äôt bad ‚Äî but make fights ~20‚Äì30% faster.

If one fight lasts longer than 8 rounds,
fatigue sets in.

4. Scavenger damage variance swung hard
You took 5 damage, then 1, then 4‚Ä¶

Early-game damage should be predictable enough that deaths feel earned, not unlucky.

Make enemy attack range tighter:

From current (I‚Äôm guessing 1‚Äì6)

To something like 2‚Äì4

If they crit?
Sure, spike it.

But right now, early-game risk swings too wildly.

5. Missing on back-to-back attacks while buffed feels bad
‚ÄúStatus: Focused‚Äù should MEAN something.

Round 2 Change Spec (simple, high impact)
Here‚Äôs what I‚Äôd have Otto do next, in order of impact vs effort.

1. Add a Graze mechanic to attacks
Goal: fewer ‚Äúdead‚Äù turns, better combat pacing.

Rule:

If Roll + AttackBonus is within 2‚Äì3 points below the target‚Äôs Defense, treat it as a Graze:

Hit for half damage (rounded up)

No on-hit effects (no bleed, no rider abilities)

Result:

You still feel like you‚Äôre wearing the enemy down, even on ‚Äúnear miss‚Äù.

Fights get ~20‚Äì30% shorter without reducing tension.

2. Tune enemy HP / damage (especially Wild Beasts)
Scavenger:

HP: 15 ‚Üí 12

Damage: keep roughly where it is (1‚Äì4 or 2‚Äì4), just avoid 0-damage jokes.

Wild Beast:

HP: 20 ‚Üí 14‚Äì16

Damage:

Reduce max from 9 down to maybe 6‚Äì7,

Or implement a ‚ÄúHeavy Hit‚Äù with lower frequency instead of random spikes.

Also:

Mark ‚ÄúClear the Den‚Äù in the mission list as:

Clear the Den (Hard ‚Äì Recommended Level 2+)

3. Make abilities punchier and clearer
Power Strike:

Give it a +2 Attack bonus AND +2 damage (or ‚Äúroll damage twice, pick higher‚Äù).

Optional: if it misses, still apply a Graze.

Brace:

Give a clear numeric effect: e.g., +4 Defense this round or disadvantage on enemy attacks.

Print it: ‚ÄúDefense increased by 4 this round.‚Äù

We want you to feel:

‚ÄúWhen I press the ability button, something big happens.‚Äù

4. First Aid fix for Pioneer

No target prompt

‚ÄúYou restore X HP‚Äù

50 (Package)

37 (failed Hack) = 87 XP

Here‚Äôs a ready-to-paste prompt you can drop into Cursor for him to make these adjustments:

Symbioz ‚Äì Round 2 tuning

Context:
We have a working CLI MVP in `apps/symbioz_cli/` with:
- 3 races (Human, Stonelock, Aeshura)
- 4 classes (Vanguard, Operative, Tech Specialist, Pioneer)
- Missions: Retrieve the Package, Hack the Terminal, Clear the Den
- D20-style combat and basic skill checks

I‚Äôve now done two full playtests:
1) Stonelock Pioneer with pistol ‚Äì died to the Scavenger once, then again due to long, whiffy combat and accidentally healing the enemy with First Aid.
2) Stonelock Vanguard with sword ‚Äì killed the Scavenger and completed mission 1; got partial success on Hack the Terminal; got wrecked in Clear the Den by two Wild Beasts hitting very hard (one hit for 9 damage on 15 HP).

Based on this, apply the following tuning changes:

1. Add a Graze mechanic
- In the combat system (`systems/combat.py`):
  - When an attack roll (d20 + attack bonus) is within 2‚Äì3 points below the target‚Äôs Defense, treat that as a ‚ÄúGraze‚Äù instead of a full miss.
  - A Graze should:
    - Deal half the normal damage (rounded up).
    - NOT apply any on-hit status effects (like bleed).
  - Log message example: `FARTZ MGOO? grazes the Scavenger for 2 damage!`
- Update `COMBAT_SYSTEM.md` to document the Graze rule so design and code stay in sync.

2. Retune early enemies (Scavenger and Wild Beast)
- Scavenger:
  - Reduce HP from 15 to 12.
  - Ensure its damage range is modest and consistent (e.g., 2‚Äì4) so level 1 characters don‚Äôt get randomly spiked down.
- Wild Beast:
  - Reduce HP from 20 to 14‚Äì16 (tune and note the final value).
  - Reduce its typical damage so it can‚Äôt hit for 9+ on level 1 characters.
  - If you want ‚Äúheavy hit‚Äù moments, model them explicitly (e.g., 20% chance to use a heavy attack) instead of pure RNG damage spikes.
- In the mission list display:
  - Label ‚ÄúClear the Den‚Äù as: `Clear the Den (Hard ‚Äì Recommended Level 2+)`.

3. Make abilities more impactful and clear
- Vanguard‚Äôs Power Strike:
  - Give it both an accuracy and damage boost.
  - For example:
    - On the next attack, add +2 to hit and +2 to damage.
  - Make sure the log reflects this: e.g., `Power Strike active! Your next attack gains +2 to hit and +2 damage.`
- Vanguard‚Äôs Brace:
  - Give a clear numeric defensive bonus, e.g., +4 Defense until the start of the next turn or disadvantage on enemy attacks.
  - Show this in the log: `FARTZ MGOO? braces! Defense increased.` with the actual numbers if possible.
- Pioneer‚Äôs Survival Instinct:
  - Confirm it meaningfully affects either attack rolls, skill checks, or both.
  - Make the buff duration and effect obvious in the status display.

4. Fix First Aid to never heal enemies in MVP
- In the ability logic:
  - For now, limit First Aid to self-targeting only.
  - Don‚Äôt prompt the user for a target; just heal the player character and log something like: `You restore X HP with First Aid.`
- Later we can add more complex targeting or ally-healing; MVP should be simple and safe.

5. Slight XP curve adjustments
- Check the XP thresholds for level-ups in `systems/progression.py`.
- For MVP:
  - Set the level 2 threshold so that:
    - Completing ‚ÄúRetrieve the Package‚Äù (50 XP) + a failed ‚ÄúHack the Terminal‚Äù run with reduced rewards (currently 37 XP) will bring a level 1 character to level 2 (e.g., threshold ~75‚Äì80 XP).
- Update any reference in the design docs if necessary.

6. Honey / item usability
- Vital Honey currently drops as an item.
- Make sure:
  - It appears in the inventory after mission 1.
  - It‚Äôs usable via ‚ÄúUse Item‚Äù in combat and actually restores HP or provides a simple buff.
  - Log a clear message when it‚Äôs used (`You consume Vital Honey and restore X HP`).
- Optionally:
  - After the first mission where Vital Honey drops, add a short hub message or hint reminding the player that items can be used during combat.

After making these changes:
- Run through a quick test with:
  - A level 1 Vanguard vs Scavenger.
  - The ‚ÄúHack the Terminal‚Äù mission with a non-Tech class.
  - ‚ÄúClear the Den‚Äù at level 1 (should feel very dangerous) and at level 2 (should feel hard but survivable with smart play and item use).
- Summarize in a short markdown file (e.g., `symbioz/MVP_TUNING_NOTES.md`) how the feel of combat and mission difficulty changed.
If you want, next round we can:

Fold in graze + tuning into the COMBAT_SYSTEM doc textually,

Or start speccing ‚Äúcompanions‚Äù so Clear the Den becomes a proper 3v2 scrap instead of a solo mauling.

But from what you‚Äôve shown:
the loop works, the fights have personality, and we‚Äôre now at the ‚Äútighten screws‚Äù stage, not the ‚Äúis this even a game‚Äù stage.

That‚Äôs a damn good place to be.

5. How Otto/Cursor can automate this

Output .txt prompts into symbioz/art_prompts/.

or use the OpenAI Images API locally with a small batch script.

The nice thing: whenever we expand races/classes, we just add YAML, run script, boom: new prompts.

### Step 1 ‚Äì Fix Tech Specialist ‚ÄúRepair‚Äù and add ‚ÄúOverload Systems‚Äù

**1.1 Repair (self-only heal)**

In the Tech Specialist ability logic (probably in `combat.py` or wherever abilities are handled):

- Ensure ‚ÄúRepair‚Äù:
  - Can only target the player character (no enemy targeting).
  - Restores HP: e.g. heal amount = `1d4 + INT modifier` (minimum 1 HP).
  - Cannot exceed max HP.
- Log message:
  - `"{name} reroutes power and stabilizes systems, restoring {healed} HP."`

Make sure we can‚Äôt accidentally heal enemies anymore. If there is currently a target selection for Repair, remove it for now and make it self-only.

**1.2 New offensive ability: Overload Systems**

- Add ‚ÄúOverload Systems‚Äù as a Tech Specialist combat ability.

Behavior:
- Player selects ‚ÄúUse Ability‚Äù ‚Üí ‚ÄúOverload Systems‚Äù.
- Choose an enemy target (for now, single target).
- Make an attack roll:
  - `d20 + INT modifier + small ability bonus (e.g. +2)` vs enemy Defense.
- On hit:
  - Deal energy damage: `1d6 + INT modifier`.
  - Apply a debuff to that enemy for 2 rounds (including this one), such as:
    - `-2 Defense` (so other attacks have a higher chance to hit).
- On miss:
  - No damage, no debuff.
- Log messages:
  - On cast: `"{name} overloads enemy systems!"`
  - On hit: `"{name}'s overload hits {enemy_name} for {damage} energy damage and disrupts their defenses!"`
  - On miss: `"{name}'s overload fizzles against {enemy_name}'s shielding."`

Update any class/ability data structures so Tech Specialist shows:
- Hack
- Repair
- Overload Systems

(If you need to drop Hack for now to keep the menu simple, keep Repair + Overload Systems as the two Tech abilities.)

Also:
- Update `COMBAT_SYSTEM.md` to document Repair and Overload Systems, including their formulas and effects.

---

### Step 2 ‚Äì Strengthen items & Vital Honey

**2.1 Vital Honey effect**

- In the item data and combat item-handling code:
  - Confirm Vital Honey is in the player‚Äôs inventory after mission rewards.
  - Define its effect as:
    - Heal `1d6 + CON modifier` HP (minimum 3 HP), OR a flat value like `6 HP` if easier.
- Ensure:
  - Vital Honey can be used during a player turn via ‚ÄúUse Item‚Äù.
  - Using it consumes one charge.
  - HP does not exceed max HP.

Log:
- `"{name} consumes Vital Honey, restoring {healed} HP."`

**2.2 Item usage hint**

- After the first mission where the player gets Vital Honey, display a brief hint at the hub or at least in the mission complete text:
  - `"Hint: You can use Vital Honey during combat via 'Use Item' to restore HP."`

### Step 3 ‚Äì Add a mid-tier combat mission

**Mission: ‚ÄúSalvage Run‚Äù**

Add a new mission to `data/missions.json`:

- ID: `salvage_run`
- Name: `Salvage Run`
- Description:  
  `"A salvage hauler broke down near the station. Escort the repair crew and fend off opportunistic threats."`
- Difficulty: between ‚ÄúRetrieve the Package‚Äù and ‚ÄúClear the Den‚Äù.
- XP reward: around `60‚Äì70`.
- Credits reward: maybe `30‚Äì40`.

Encounter design:
- Either:
  - 2 moderate enemies (e.g. ‚ÄúRaider‚Äù with ~10‚Äì12 HP, modest damage),  
  OR
  - 1 slightly tougher enemy (e.g. ‚ÄúArmored Scavenger‚Äù with higher Defense but lower damage per hit).
- Tune so:
  - A level 1 character *can* win with good play and some luck,
  - A level 2 character feels appropriately challenged but not overwhelmed.

Update the mission selection menu to include ‚ÄúSalvage Run‚Äù as Mission 2 or 3 (depending on ordering), with a brief description and XP reward.

### Step 4 ‚Äì Implement a simple Vendor

Activate the ‚ÄúVisit Vendor‚Äù option at the Outpost:

**Vendor inventory:**
- Improved Pistol
- Improved Sword
- Reinforced Light Armor
- Vital Honey (single-use or small stack, optional)

Define items:

- Improved Pistol:
  - Same as Basic Pistol but:
    - +1 to hit OR +1 damage.
- Improved Sword:
  - Same as Basic Sword but:
    - +1 damage.
- Reinforced Light Armor:
  - +1 Defense over the base armor.

**Pricing:**
- Choose reasonable prices so:
  - After 2‚Äì3 missions, the player can afford at least ONE upgrade.
  - Example:  
    - Improved Pistol: 80 credits  
    - Improved Sword: 80 credits  
    - Reinforced Light Armor: 70 credits  
    - Vital Honey: 25 credits each

**Behavior:**
- Show a simple menu:
  - List items with price.
  - Show player credits.
- On purchase:
  - If player has enough credits:
    - Deduct cost.
    - Equip weapon/armor immediately.
    - Or add item (Vital Honey) to inventory.
  - Otherwise:
    - Show ‚ÄúNot enough credits.‚Äù

Update `main.py` vendor handling code to implement this menu and purchasing logic.

Let‚Äôs build some Symbioz lore
Let‚Äôs treat this like the start of symbioz/design/LORE_BIBLE.md.

I‚Äôll give you tight, usable chunks, not a 40-page novel.

1. The high concept of the setting
Symbioz is set on the ragged edge of a half-settled star region called the Amber Reach ‚Äî a cluster of systems where reality bends around a strange, ancient substance: Amber.

Most people think Amber is just another exotic resource. They‚Äôre wrong. It‚Äôs the visible residue of something older and weirder that nobody fully understands.

Out here you‚Äôve got:

Corporate combines strip-mining asteroids

Honey cartels quietly becoming more powerful than governments

Fractured planetary governments trying to control trade routes

Strange, rare ‚ÄúChannelers‚Äù (NPC-only) who can bend Amber in ways that look like magic

You and your crew are just a small piece in that mess:

running jobs,

making enemies,

trying not to get eaten by beasts or honey mutations.

2. Honey & Amber ‚Äì how it actually works
We already decided:

Honey = the everyday, tangible expression of planetary weirdness.

Amber = the rare, almost mystical shit.

Let‚Äôs pin that down:

Honey
Each planet has its own mix of pollen / spores / microflora.

Bees (or equivalent species / engineered swarms) ingest that, and the resulting Honey carries:

trace Amber signatures,

biochemical quirks,

sometimes straight-up psychoactive effects.

In game terms:

Common Honey strains:

Vital Honey ‚Äì boosts healing/regeneration.

Steady Honey ‚Äì small defense/accuracy buff, minimal side effects.

Rare strains:

Frenzy Honey ‚Äì massive attack buff, but post-combat crash or HP penalty.

Glass Honey ‚Äì huge skill/psionic-like boost, but HP or armor penalties.

The ‚Äúbrewing‚Äù side:

Pioneers, Tech Specialists, certain races can:

combine 2‚Äì3 strains,

stabilize them,

craft items that sit between medicine and narcotic.

This is where your crafting trees will eventually live.

Amber
Found in weird crystalline growths or embedded in old wreckage.

Unstable but powerful ‚Äî raw Amber is dangerous to non-Channelers.

Real ‚Äúmagic‚Äù (Channeling) needs:

a Channeler NPC,

Amber,

some kind of ritual/tech interface.

For now, Amber is mostly:

story hooks,

high-tier upgrade material,

explanation for WTF tech.

3. Big-picture factions (hooks for missions)
Here are three core factions we can build on later.

3.1 The Confluence Cartel
‚ÄúWe don‚Äôt grow Honey. We curate it.‚Äù

A loose syndicate of ‚Äúbusiness-minded‚Äù smugglers and refiners.

Control most long-range Honey trade.

Publicly: respectable logistics & agritech corporation.

Privately: flooded half the Reach with addictive strains.

Game hooks:

Smuggling runs,

Price-fixing operations,

Sabotage or blackmail jobs,

Access to high-tier Honey if you get in deep.

3.2 The Wardens of the Reach
‚ÄúWe were never asked to be police. We were forced into it.‚Äù

A quasi-religious, quasi-military order.

Try to keep Amber incidents from escalating into system-wide disasters.

Seen as meddlers by corporations, terrorists by cartels, heroes by frontier colonies.

Game hooks:

Stop Honey mutations or beast outbreaks,

Protect settlements,

Moral-choice missions:

side with Wardens or betray them for better pay.

3.3 Horizon Combine
‚ÄúIf it can be sold, we will own it.‚Äù

Classic megacorp with:

mining fleets,

research labs,

private security,

PR arm.

Officially: bring order and infrastructure.

Unofficially: experiment on Honey/Amber and local populations.

Game hooks:

Heists,

inside jobs,

corporate black projects,

‚Äúclean up your mess‚Äù contracts.

4. One key location to anchor early missions
Let‚Äôs name the hub you‚Äôve been imagining:

Outpost K-77 ‚ÄúThe Spindle‚Äù

Semi-legal waystation near a busted warp node.

Built on the skeleton of an old war platform.

Owned on paper by Horizon Combine, effectively run day-to-day by whoever has the most guns that week.

Your ‚ÄúThe Outpost‚Äù hub is basically a deck in the Spindle.

Features:

Docking ring full of patched-together ships.

Honey dens disguised as ‚Äútea houses.‚Äù

A Warden listening post hiding as a medical clinic.

Combine office pretending they still control anything.

This gives you:

Mission board,

Vendor,

contacts from all three big factions without leaving home.

5. Lore for your Tech Specialist (Aeshura) + Pioneers
Let‚Äôs give some race + class lore you can feel while you play.

Aeshura (race snapshot)
Graceful, slightly elongated humanoids from low-gravity ocean/reef worlds.

Sensory organs tuned to subtle vibrations and EM noise:

excellent at precision work,

decent at dodging,

physically fragile.

Cultural bits:

Treat Honey as medicine/ritual, not just commodity.

Creeped out by raw Amber; old legends say ‚Äúthe sky used to bleed light‚Äù when Amber storms came.

Why they make good Tech Specialists:

Naturally good spatial + pattern reasoning.

Comfortable with sensory overload from UIs and implants.

Viewed by others as spooky but reliable.

Pioneers (class snapshot)
Ex-rangers / survivalists / planetary fixers.

Know which plants feed you, which ones kill you, and which ones make you see the songs in Amber.

In the lore:

Early Pioneers kept outposts like the Spindle alive during the first rough years.

Modern Pioneers are kind of undervalued ‚Äúblue collar demigods‚Äù ‚Äì everyone needs them, nobody wants to pay them properly.
